Current Commentary

Crisis and Unity 43

— Star

When Mr. Hu Hanmin returned from Europe, the entire nation welcomed him. The crisis is so severe now that the party members and the people of the country have high expectations for Mr. Hu. Therefore, their welcome was very sincere. According to recent news, Mr. Hu has agreed to arrive in Nanjing from Hong Kong at the beginning of next month to assume the position of Chairman of the Standing Committee of the Central Executive Committee. At this time, public opinion is abuzz with discussions, and the political situation north of the Yellow River is completely different. The possibility of a major international war is greater than at any time since 1919. Mr. Hu resolutely comes north to shoulder the heavy responsibility of the central government and lead the people to seek a way out. This is truly a good sign of unity and saving the nation.

Looking at various nations in times of crisis and survival, there are always two or three leaders who bravely step forward to guide the people and prevent the destruction of a race or a country. The unification of Italy, breaking away from the oppression of Austria and creating the glory of a new Rome, was due to the efforts of the three heroes: Cavour, Garibaldi, and Mazzini. The independence of the United States, breaking away from the rule of England and laying the foundation for the United States of America, was due to the efforts of Washington, Jefferson, and Hamilton. The success of the Russian Revolution and the progress of nation-building were due to the three leaders: Lenin, Trotsky, and Stalin. And France was able to overcome its difficulties during the European War mainly due to the efforts of Clemenceau, Poincaré, and Briand. These nation-building leaders mostly had different ideas and beliefs. Garibaldi was a military man, Cavour was a politician, and the two were often incompatible and indulged in their own opinions. However, Garibaldi eventually abandoned his prejudices and handed over southern Italy to the unified Italian government. Jefferson and Hamilton were one a proponent of decentralization and the other a proponent of centralization, and they attacked each other and could not compromise. Thanks to Washington's proper coordination, one was in charge of foreign affairs and the other in charge of finance, each working hard for the new country. As for Trotsky and Stalin in Soviet Russia, their political differences were too great to allow them to cooperate. During the European War, the three major French politicians were also at odds with each other, but they all made significant contributions to their country.

The leadership of the new Chinese politics lies with the Chinese Nationalist Party, and since the death of Mr. Sun Yat-sen, Chiang Kai-shek, Hu Hanmin, and Wang Jingwei have been publicly recognized as the most prestigious and capable leaders in the party. In the past, the three leaders have also been unable to get along due to differences in opinions, with someone leaving and someone else taking over in rotation. This has happened many times, and each change has made us realize the necessity of unity and cooperation among the leaders. The success of party rule depends on the proper guidance of the leaders, and Chiang, Wang, and Hu each have their strengths in military affairs, party affairs, and politics, and none can be neglected. The difference in their political views is not comparable to that between Jefferson and Hamilton, and the difference in their personalities is even less like that between Cavour and Garibaldi. Moreover, they all shared hardships with Mr. Sun, and their past work was aimed at fulfilling Mr. Sun's legacy. At this time, the national crisis has entered its most urgent stage, and no one can avoid the feeling that it is difficult to support a collapsing building with a single beam. Now that Mr. Hu has decided to go to Nanjing to take office, and it is said that Mr. Wang will also go to the capital to serve as soon as his injuries are slightly better, if the three can sincerely cooperate and jointly seek to save the current crisis, then this will not only be a sign of the great unity of the Nationalist Party, but also a glimmer of hope for the future of the nation.

US House Foreign Affairs Committee Passes New Neutrality Bill; Original Bill Slightly Amended 44

Washington The House Foreign Affairs Committee today passed the government's neutrality bill and submitted it to the House. The bill stipulates a mandatory ban on the export of munitions and allows the president to decide whether to ban the export of wartime materials beyond the normal needs of the importing country. The bill also contains a provision prohibiting loans or credit to belligerent countries. (National Telegraph, 27th)

Washington The House Foreign Affairs Committee today passed the neutrality bill but deleted the clause giving the president the power to prohibit the export of goods that he deems would prolong the war if not prohibited. The chairman of the Foreign Affairs Committee stated that the bill will be submitted to the House in the middle of this week or early next week. The Senate Foreign Affairs Committee is still unable to reconcile its opinions on the bill, because Senators Borah and Johnson are vigorously advocating for more powerful guarantees of freedom of the seas. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

Washington The House Foreign Affairs Committee has completed a report on the new neutrality bill proposed by Committee Chairman McReynolds, and has slightly amended the original bill. The main points of the report are: The provisions of the new neutrality bill should not be applied to Central and South American countries when wars occur between them and countries outside the Americas. The export of medicines and food to belligerent countries should be prohibited, as determined by the president. Americans who violate the new neutrality law and lend short-term or long-term loans to belligerent countries will be imprisoned or fined $50,000. If the content of treaties signed between the United States and other countries conflicts with the new neutrality law, the president should negotiate with the countries concerned before changing the treaties. If these negotiations fail, the president may declare the treaty abolished. The new neutrality law should be implemented as soon as the treaty expires. (Havas dispatch, 27th)

Severe Cold Wave Sweeps Through the United States; Atlantic Coast Almost Entirely Covered in Ice; Niagara Falls Freezes Over, Unprecedented 45

Chicago The United States, from the Rocky Mountains to the Atlantic coast, is almost entirely covered in ice. The Arctic cold has been felt for a week. Since Wednesday, 235 people have frozen to death. Ohio has the highest number of deaths, with 47 people. Waterways in Ohio are all frozen, and transportation is completely blocked, which has not happened since 1918. The famous Niagara Falls has been frozen for three days now, which is unprecedented. The cold weather in the Midwestern states has broken all 20th-century records. The cold wave is now in its second week and is expected to continue for three more days. Only Florida and the Pacific coast have slightly warmer climates. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

New York Temperatures east of the Rocky Mountains have been below zero degrees for six days. There have been numerous deaths in the affected areas, and efforts are being made to alleviate the suffering of the people. An Associated Press reporter learned today that the cold wave has severely affected the Southeast, with at least 230 people frozen to death. Furthermore, there are concerns about coal shortages in Iowa, Wisconsin, Indiana, and Illinois, which is exacerbating the disaster. Coal sales have increased sharply due to the continued severe cold, and all coal stocks have been sold out, resulting in coal production failing to meet demand. The number of deaths in each state is as follows: Ohio 48, Pennsylvania 29, Illinois 28, New York 19, Michigan 16, Wisconsin 12, Minnesota 11, Iowa 7, Kentucky 7, Massachusetts 7, Indiana 26, West Virginia 5, Alabama, Connecticut, Nebraska, Texas, and Kansas, one each, Missouri 3, Maine 2. (National Telegraph, 27th)

Ten Thousand Spectators Line the Streets of London; Former King George Laid to Rest; Cannons and Church Bells Resound Together; Procession Takes One Hour to Pass 46

London Starting from 9 p.m. last night, all the main streets in London that the hearse would pass through were already occupied. Some people spread newspapers on the sidewalks and lay down to wait for dawn, while others gathered under the eaves. Some even brought cots to the street corners. Fortunately, the rain had stopped, and the weather was still mild at night. Pedestrians kept coming and going all night, but it was extremely quiet and orderly. By 5 a.m. this morning, the streets were packed with people. The windows and doors of various residences in the Oxford and Cambridge areas were removed and bleachers were built. All organizations were decorated with black and purple, black to express mourning and purple because the royal color is purple.

The crowds lining the streets along the route of the hearse were silent. Men took off their hats with sad expressions, and women mostly wore mourning clothes, standing with their heads bowed. Compared with the scene last year when celebrating the 25th anniversary of the king's accession to the throne, when every household hung flags and everyone cheered, the contrast between joy and sorrow is truly stark. The flagpoles used to hang flags in the streets during last year's celebration were erected again today, but they were all hung with mourning flags trimmed with black ropes.

Those crowding the windows, balconies, and specially built bleachers were all dressed in black. In Hyde Park, 600 British soldiers holding sixty flags and soldiers from other countries gave the final salute as the hearse passed. Soldiers were lined up on both sides of the streets. Behind the hearse, in addition to eight carriages carrying British and foreign royal ladies, the pallbearers all walked on foot. The Queen Mother sat in the first carriage.

As the hearse approached Marble Arch, the crowds became too dense and broke through the police line. With the help of auxiliary police, the police were still unable to make the crowd retreat. After the cavalry drove them away, the police line was restored. The commotion lasted for several minutes, and at least dozens of men and women were injured and sent to the hospital. When the hearse arrived, the police quickly used loudspeakers to ask the people behind not to push forward anymore. This move was very effective, and order was restored. As the procession passed Marble Arch, a sudden rain shower fell, but it cleared up quickly.

The hearse traveled safely all the way to Paddington Station. According to Reuters reporters, since this morning, there has been no space on the streets and sidewalks. The police ordered women carrying young children to stand in the front row. The order of the crowds everywhere was good, except for Marble Arch, where the overcrowding caused many people to faint. According to statistics, 800 people were treated at nearby first aid stations.

At 9:20 a.m., King Edward of England and his three brothers entered Westminster Abbey. At 9:30 a.m., cannons boomed, mixed with the sounds of church bells. The procession then set off in succession at 9:49 a.m. At this time, the sun broke through the clouds, and the coffin was covered with the royal flag. The procession paused twice as it approached the corner of Hyde Park.

London's commerce was temporarily suspended at this time, and almost all Londoners gathered at the locations along the procession route. It was as if the city was empty. Except for a slight setback at Marble Arch, everything proceeded in order. After one hour and eight minutes, the entire procession had passed. Prime Minister Baldwin did not serve as a pallbearer and follow along. He had already gone to Windsor with several cabinet members and foreign representatives. As the special train carrying the coffin passed over the Thames River Bridge, the Tower of London began to ring its bell, once per minute, for a total of 101 times. According to custom, the bell of this tower is only rung when the monarch is laid to rest. (Reuters dispatch, 28th)

Windsor The mourning decorations here today are the same as in London. Soldiers were densely deployed on both sides of the station and on the main road leading to St. George's Chapel. Spectators were packed like a wall, all standing quietly behind the soldiers. In the early morning, important people such as cabinet members arrived in Windsor. The special train carrying the coffin did not arrive until 1:08 p.m., 33 minutes later than scheduled. It was said that the procession was slightly delayed due to the crowds of spectators, which caused the train to be unable to depart on time. After the special train arrived, the coffin was immediately carried down and moved onto a gun carriage, leaving the station at 1:01 p.m. King Edward of England walked behind with his head bowed. Mountains of wreaths were piled up in St. George's Chapel. After the coffin was carried into the church, King Edward stood in front of the coffin, the Queen Mother to his right, and the royal family behind them. Then, a hymn was sung, and the coffin was carried into the tomb and slowly lowered into the grave. King Edward stepped forward and sprinkled soil from the grave onto the coffin. Then, there was a silent pause of two minutes. The time was 2:10 p.m., 40 minutes later than scheduled. After the silence, the national anthem was sung, and a prayer of blessing was performed. After the ceremony, King Edward and the Queen Mother slowly walked out of the church, took a car to the train station, and returned to London. (Reuters dispatch, 28th)

A Glimpse of the Funeral Procession: Escorted by Six Kings and Twenty-Seven Princes, Thirty-Three Envoys 47

The funeral ceremony of the late King George V of London was held this morning, a spectacle rarely seen in Britain. The coffin departed from Westminster Hall and proceeded to Paddington Station for transport to Windsor for burial. Besides the full military honors, six kings (including King Edward VIII), twenty-seven princes, thirty-three ambassadors or ministers, and fifty detachments of troops from various countries accompanied the procession. Crowds in mourning attire stood solemnly along the streets the procession was scheduled to pass from early morning, awaiting its arrival. When the royal guards carried the late King's coffin from Westminster Hall, the crowds on both sides of the road stood silently and motionless. King Edward VIII and his three brothers arrived at the church around 9:45 AM. The honor guard, composed of soldiers from the army, navy, and air force, saluted the King. Subsequently, artillerymen placed the late King's coffin on a gun carriage. The King was dressed in the uniform of an Admiral of the Fleet, his brothers the Duke of York in the uniform of an Air Force officer of the Royal Air Force, the Duke of Gloucester in the uniform of a Colonel of the Hussars, and the Duke of Kent in the uniform of a naval officer. The coffin was draped with a gold and red royal standard, adorned with red and white roses offered by Queen Mary. At that moment, Hyde Park began firing salutes, which lasted for seventy minutes. As soon as the salutes began, the funeral procession formed into line according to the predetermined order. When the hearse set off, the radio station immediately broadcast the signal, which was relayed by the police, and the entire procession began to move. The weather this morning was originally gloomy, but at this moment it suddenly cleared up, and the sun shone brightly. As for the order of the procession, it was led by a staff officer, followed by dozens of British troops and thirty-one detachments of foreign troops. Next came a staff officer, naval officers, and a band. The Duke of Norfolk, the Minister in charge of funeral arrangements, led the royal officials and courtiers following the band. Then came the hearse, drawn by 142 naval sailors, followed by a court attendant carrying the royal standard. King Edward walked behind, with a sorrowful expression, followed by his brothers and royal relatives, including King Haakon III of Norway (the late King's brother-in-law), Crown Prince Olav of Norway, and Count Helhuth (the late King's son-in-law). Next came President Lebrun of France, King Christian of Denmark, and King Carol of Romania, the three heads of state walking abreast. Further back were other princes, such as Crown Prince Umberto of Italy, Crown Prince Charles of Sweden, Crown Prince Paul of Greece, Austrian Vice-Chancellor Prince Starhemberg, and Regent Paul of Yugoslavia, all following the heads of state. Queen Mary, Queen Maud of Norway (the late King's sister), the Duchess of York (the late King's daughter-in-law), and Princess Helhuth rode in black carriages drawn by brown horses. Behind them were diplomatic envoys from various countries and representatives of the autonomous territories, as well as seven royal carriages carrying the former Queen of Spain, the Duchess of Gloucester, the Duchess of Kent, and Princess Connaught (the daughter of the late King's eldest sister). Finally came the delegations from various countries and a detachment of the Royal Guards. (Havas dispatch, 28th)

The late King George V of London was buried today, and the Chinese government specially sent its ambassador to Britain, Guo Taiqi, to represent the country in escorting the coffin. The Japanese government sent its ambassador to France, Saito, to participate. Both Chinese and Japanese ambassadors walked with the heads of government of various countries following the coffin. (Havas dispatch, 28th)

The British church in Rome held a memorial service for the late King George V of England at 10:50 AM this morning. King Emmanuel and Prime Minister Mussolini both attended. (Havas dispatch, 28th)

The Church of St. George in Berlin held a memorial service for the late King George V of England this morning. Führer Hitler also attended. (Havas dispatch, 28th)

The funeral ceremony of the former King George V of London will be held today with the honor befitting an Admiral of the Navy. At 9:45 AM this morning, the hearse will depart from Westminster Abbey. At that time, the entire city will be in complete silence. The only sounds to break the silence will be the salutes from Hyde Park and the Tower of London, and the sound of tens of thousands of people escorting the coffin. The gold coffin will be placed on a gun carriage, drawn by the navy, and will travel approximately four miles through the streets of London to Paddington Station. Then, the gold coffin will be transferred to a special train to Windsor. Following the gun carriage on foot will be the new King Edward, followed by the British royal family and foreign royal family members. The Queen Mother will follow in a carriage. The foreign monarchs walking and escorting the coffin will include the monarchs of Belgium, Denmark, Norway, Bulgaria, and Romania. Preceding the gun carriage will be army and navy troops, stretching for a mile. The troops will march with their rifles reversed. Following the troops will be high-ranking officials from various departments, as well as military bands and flute bands. When the hearse departs from Westminster Abbey, Hyde Park and the Tower of London will fire salutes, one every minute, until the hearse reaches Paddington Station. It is estimated that the journey will take two hours. After the special train arrives at Windsor Station, the gold coffin will be transferred to another gun carriage and taken to St. George's Chapel for burial. Whenever the gold coffin is moved, the flute band will play music. When the burial ceremony is completed, the entire nation will observe two minutes of silence. There will be many spectators along the route taken by the hearse. The authorities have made arrangements in advance, and all streets along the route will be closed to traffic from 8:00 AM. The cinemas will open at 6:00 PM, and it is expected that major cinemas will screen new films of today's funeral ceremony. Last night, Windsor Palace received approximately 1,500 wreaths from all over the world, from monarchs to ordinary people. Among them were those sent by our country's emperors, such as the Japanese Emperor, the Italian King, the Afghan King, and the deposed German Emperor, which were exquisitely crafted and showed the utmost skill of the florists. Last night, the Queen Mother also visited Westminster Abbey and stood beside the coffin for several minutes, accompanied by members of the British royal family and foreign royal relatives. While the Queen Mother and others were in the abbey, public viewing was temporarily suspended. The monarchs of Denmark and Belgium, the President of France, and the three or four princes of Sweden, Italy, and Greece all arrived in England yesterday, and were welcomed by British officials. On the last day of public viewing, mourners continued to arrive in an endless stream. Despite the rain all day, the crowds did not diminish. At one point, those standing along the route waiting to enter the abbey reached three miles in length, so the abbey doors did not close until 4:00 AM this morning. (Reuters dispatch, 28th)

U.S. Silver Purchase Policy Fails; Britain Eager to Promote the Weakening of Silver's Position 60

Washington: The leader of the silver faction in the House of Representatives stated today that they have abandoned the hope of passing any bills in this congressional session that would enhance the status of silver. Democratic Congressman Martin said that silver faction members may soon hold a meeting to discuss this matter, but he fears that there will be no practical results. Martin believes that the failure of the Treasury Department's silver purchase policy is due to the cool attitude of Treasury Secretary Morgenthau. If the Secretary does not allow Britain to deceive him, the status of silver will not be as it is today. If he could have declared to Britain that the Treasury Department would purchase silver as much as possible, then Britain's anti-silver propaganda would not have materialized. China and India have both been incited by Britain. Britain has been opposing silver for 120 years. Therefore, after the United States implemented the silver purchase policy, Britain has tried every possible means to weaken the status of silver and reduce the exchange rate of the gold pound against Asian currencies in order to establish a connection between the gold pound and Far Eastern currencies. At the same time, it uses a balancing fund to secure its domestic currency price. A few days after the United States stopped purchasing silver, the silver purchase policy was irreversible. (National Telegram, 27th)

But the environment in which the Democratic Party finds itself today is indeed the same as the Democratic Party in 1896, that is, there is a force within it that firmly wants to raise the silver price to a ratio of 1 to 16, while another faction opposes it. President Bryan leaned toward the silver faction, calling for free silver coinage, which resulted in an unprecedented defeat. And Roosevelt's current situation is very similar to this, so the magnitude of the crisis is self-evident. (National Telegram, 27th)

U.S. Bonus Bill Passes; Congress Overrides Presidential Veto; Raising Huge Sums by Three Ways 62

Washington: The U.S. Senate today overturned the President's veto of the veterans' bonus bill by a vote of 76 to 19. The bill will immediately become law, and the 15-year struggle of European War veterans to immediately pay their bonus bonds in cash has also succeeded. The majority in the Senate overriding the President's veto was not much different from the 79 votes that passed the original bill, which is the biggest decision failure since the President took office in 1933. A similar bill was also passed in the last Congress. After the President's veto, the Senate had passed a resolution in favor of the President's veto. Today, the situation has completely reversed, which shows not only that the pressure of propaganda for this bill this year is significant, but also that the point of contention over currency inflation is imminent. It is reported that the Treasury Department has begun preparing to print bonds to pay the bonus, with a face value of $50 per bond, but they will not be issued until June 16th. These bonds are scheduled to mature in 1945, but can be redeemed at any time. If all the bonds are completely redeemed, the government must prepare 2,237 million yuan in cash. It is not yet certain how this huge sum will be raised today. It is likely that it will be raised by increasing national debt, implementing new taxes, or inflating the currency. The original bill proposed by Harrison did not specify a fundraising method. (National Telegram, 27th)

American Plan: Building Streamlined Mail Ships to Dominate the Atlantic Shipping Industry 68

Washington – According to what our reporter has learned, the U.S. Department of Commerce is currently planning to build two super mail ships to navigate the Atlantic Ocean, aiming to surpass France's "Normandie" and Britain's "Queen Mary." Details about the characteristics of these mail ships are still difficult to ascertain. However, judging from the published draft plans, the new ship's design will emphasize streamlining. Impressions of Traveling North: Special Correspondent Geng Ya 69

Shandong, in ancient times, was the land of Qi and Lu, the home of sages and worthies, with many famous scenic spots and historical sites. The most prominent of these, such as the Confucius Cemetery in Qufu, Mount Tai in Tai'an, and the Three Wonders of Jinan, are all located along the Tianjin-Pukou Railway line. The Confucius Cemetery is located three li north of Qufu city, with ancient cypress trees lining the road, captivating visitors. Confucius' tomb is fifteen feet high and forty steps in circumference, with towering cypresses and a solemn atmosphere. There is a stele that reads "Tomb of the Perfectly Accomplished Sage, King Wenxuan." Within the city is also the Confucius Temple, with majestic and magnificent halls adorned with brilliant colors. The stone pillars in the Dacheng Hall are carved with dragons, baring their teeth and brandishing their claws, protruding five or six inches, their postures seemingly about to move. The three cypress trees that Confucius personally planted, one of which is in the southeast corner of the Apricot Altar, are known as the Reborn Cypress. Records state that it withered in the third year of Yongning during the Jin Dynasty and revived in the first year of Yining during the Sui Dynasty. It withered and flourished several times thereafter. During the fifteenth year of Hongzhi in the Ming Dynasty, it was again destroyed by fire, leaving only the trunk. New branches grew in the tenth year of Yongzheng during the Qing Dynasty and still exist today. The reporter once visited this place and saw that the new branches were replanted. The remaining trunk, damaged by fire, is covered with a glass罩 to prevent it from decaying. Mount Tai is one of the Five Sacred Mountains, with pine trees, clouds, springs, rocks, perilous cliffs, and secluded ravines, each possessing its own unique characteristics, inspiring admiration. The highest peak is called the Peak of Viewing the Sun. At dawn, one can witness the sunrise. As the sun emerges, the rosy glow is magnificent. The earlier one sees the sun, the more extraordinary the view. Therefore, those who climb Mount Tai must witness the sunrise to their heart's content. Currently, some disaster victims reside in the temples at the foot of the mountain, numbering 4,000 from the entire county. They are all allocated from disaster areas such as Juancheng County. Food rations are distributed based on acreage, with six liang levied per mu per month, accumulating over time to a considerable amount. Women are sometimes abducted and flee, and men also request to become monks or Daoists. The shelter strictly prohibits them from entering and leaving freely, and they sing storytelling ballads to pass the time. According to investigations, there are a total of eighty-eight cities and counties in Shandong Province that have established shelters for disaster victims, accommodating over 340,000 people. However, there are still 1.8 million people registered and awaiting relief who are without clothing or food. As the ancients said, "A people's hunger is like one's own hunger, and a people's drowning is like one's own drowning." As human beings with round heads and strong feet, we have a natural duty to help and assist each other. Wealthy people who live in comfort and luxury should not isolate themselves and abandon their rightful duty. The Three Wonders of Jinan—Daming Lake, Thousand Buddha Mountain, and Baotu Spring—I had visited several times in the past. This time, upon alighting from the train, I visited them again. Daming Lake is located in the northwest corner of the city, covering dozens of acres. The lake water does not freeze in winter (the Yellow River freezes thick in winter, allowing passage for vehicles, because of its long course and cold nature). It is as clear as a mirror. In summer, lotus leaves dance in the wind, and lotus flowers bloom in the sun, presenting a scene of boundless green connecting to the sky and thousands of reds emerging from the water. The temples and pavilions include the Lixia Pavilion, Beiji Pavilion, Huiquan Temple, Baihua Causeway, and the ancestral halls of Zhang, Tie, Zeng, and Li. Currently, many disaster victims also reside in the ancestral halls, suffering from cold and hunger. From the west city gate, one can reach the Beiji Pavilion by walking on the city wall road (commonly known as the Ring City Road, accessible by cars), passing through the northwest castle, where there is a pavilion with no plaques or couplets. However, one feels a hidden radiance of blood, said to commemorate the achievements of defending the city during the May Third Incident, symbolizing the intention to deeply engrave it in one's heart. Thousand Buddha Mountain is located two or three li south of the city, with lush pines and cypresses, and a serene and secluded landscape. Ascending hundreds of stone steps, one reaches the mountain temple. The disaster victims who lived in the temple have just been moved elsewhere. If one climbs higher, the view expands, offering an unobstructed view of the Yellow River and the cityscape. Baotu Spring is, like Daming Lake, a scenic spot in the city. In "Travels of Lao Can," Jinan is described as "every household with spring water, every door with willows," captivating readers with the beauty of the city's forests and springs. There are countless springs in Jinan, but only seventy-two are famous, with Baotu Spring being the foremost. Baotu Spring has two or three large springs (previously only three large springs) gushing out of the ground, overturning the pond water, reaching a foot or so high, with jade-like splashes and jumping pearls, resembling glittering stars and precious pagodas. Currently, the spring is being converted into tap water, using the original large spring in the West Pond and drilling three small springs in the East Pond to provide viewing for tourists. However, the scenery and layout have changed, and the original South Pond, Pearl Spring, resembling hanging grapes or broken strands of pearls, each rolling and floating on the water, was truly beautiful. Unfortunately, this time when I visited, it had been buried by the tap water reservoir. The north and south of the spring are marketplaces, lined with shops selling various goods. Although there are many tourists, there are very few customers. Many of the male disaster victims mingle among them, some with their hands tied behind their backs, wandering aimlessly, others staring at the market stalls, standing for a long time without leaving, with sunken eyes and a dull gaze, their clothes not warm enough, although there are no white cloth strips marking them, one can tell what kind of people they are. Some of the disaster victims live in the provincial government, originally allocated from the chairman's office building, receiving relatively comprehensive relief. They are regularly given the opportunity to watch a play once a week, which is greatly envied by the local poor. However, the disaster victims themselves do not sincerely wish to live as dependents, and their daily lives from the fields are contented with adhering to old ways. As the saying goes, "A golden nest, a silver nest, can't compare to one's own poor nest." Now that the breach has not been closed, there is no prospect of returning home, and their inner anxiety and suffering are truly unimaginable by others.

6. The Yellow River Breach and Closing the Breach

The upper and middle reaches of the Yellow River rush through mountain valleys, carrying mud and sand. In the lower reaches, they are deposited everywhere. Shandong is located in the lowermost reaches of the Yellow River. As the river flows lower, it becomes more winding and prone to siltation, making the river channel from the border of Hebei to the sea, over 800 li long, almost impossible to defend step by step. It is generally considered a dangerous engineering site. This is truly another great threat facing Shandong, and a serious problem awaiting fundamental remediation. Last July, due to heavy rainfall in the upper reaches of the Yellow River, the water level rose, the river channel was shallow, and the levees were not strong. For various reasons, six breaches occurred in the southern levee at Dongzhuang in Juancheng, The water flowed from west to east. The first to fourth breaches were quickly silted up, with a total width of 430 meters. The fifth and sixth breaches merged into one, with a width exceeding 1,800 meters. The amount of water flowing out of the breach was initially 60% of the total river flow, then increased to 80%, and recently increased to 99%. Because the terrain outside the dike is lower than the riverbed, the water flows downwards without any obstruction. Therefore, the main river channel below the breach is becoming increasingly shallow.

Page 11

At the beginning of the breach, the total river flow reached 14,000 cubic meters per second. By winter, it had dropped to only 1,000 cubic meters per second. The amount flowing down the main river channel was less than 10 cubic meters per second, with a depth of only one meter (equivalent to just over one chi) and a width of twenty meters. If left to its natural course, there is a risk of it drying up completely. The water overflowing from the breach flooded seventeen counties in western Shandong and northern Jiangsu. If the breach-closing project is delayed, the disaster area may expand further. The loss, calculated solely based on regular and miscellaneous tax revenue in western Shandong, has already sharply decreased by 7.4 million yuan. The total value of other public and private property that has been submerged is more than ten or a hundred times that amount. Regarding the breach-closing project, first, the Jiangsu dam was extended into the river to shift the flow northward. Also, dredging and guiding water work was done at the silted corner inside the main river channel, using the backflow force of the dam head to scour the bay and recover some of the floodwater. Then, another diversion canal was dug along the main river channel, and the new dike of the Jiangsu dam was extended to the riverbank. Waiting for the ice flood period to arrive, the force of the ice water rise will be used to pick up the flow and introduce it into the main river channel, reducing the breach floodwater. Before the flood season, arrangements will be made to close the eastern and western dams. Currently, more than 3,000 disaster victims are engaged in this work, which shows the immensity of the project. Therefore, on the other hand, based on the many bends in the main river channel, the high riverbed, the small flow rate, and the vastness of the breach-closing project, public opinion deeply regrets that Li Yizhi's plan to dig a diversion canal in the lower reaches was not adopted. However, in fact, it is too late to regret it. It is better to continue with the breach-closing plan, without looking back, and actively complete it. Then, a comprehensive plan can be made, the root cause can be addressed, and a complete water conservancy project can be implemented to achieve the goal of long-term peace and stability. I recall that after the great flood of the twentieth year, it was followed by the outbreak of the September 18th Incident. Last autumn, the whole country suffered another great flood, and a serious problem arose in North China. This is somewhat similar to the story of the State of Yue rising up and annexing the State of Wu during a year of severe famine in the Warring States period. We cannot ignore a major cause simply because the problem is not that simple. I believe that the government's stated goal of internal pacification, truly for the practical benefit of the nation, should prioritize actively building water conservancy and passively eradicating corruption over other tasks. Although this may seem like commonplace talk, it is still a thought-provoking argument in terms of practical needs.

7. From Jinan to Beiping, the Tianjin-Pukou Railway is 1,069 kilometers long. From Pukou to Jinan, 657 kilometers have already been traveled. Only 412 kilometers remain to Tianjin, and it will be reached the morning after leaving in the evening. The train departs from Jinan and quickly passes the Yellow River Railway Bridge, which is 1,300 meters long (about three Chinese li), the greatest structure on the line. If the upper reaches of the Yellow River had not breached, looking down at the turbulent waves would have broadened the traveler's mind. Now, the excessive overflow from the breach means that the flow is less than one or two percent of the original flow. The flow is slow and steady and has long since frozen over, covered with yellow dust, no different from the open fields. If traveling for the first time after the breach, without someone pointing it out, one would only see the steel beams of the railway bridge passing by through the car windows, without hearing the sound of the Yellow River rushing eastward. Few would believe that it is the famous Yellow River, and some might even feel that the railway bridge is a waste of talent and resources. There are three mountains nearby. One is Mount Que, a giant mountain with craggy rocks, lined up on the north bank of the Yellow River. From a distance, it resembles a magpie standing sideways. One is Mount Biao, located five li south of the bridge, standing tall like a landmark. One is Mount Hua, located eight or nine li east of the bridge, facing Mount Que, resembling a flower dream. Li Bai climbed and toured it and wrote the line, "How towering this mountain is, its green like a lotus flower." After passing this, one goes straight to the capital of Yan, with vast plains and an unobstructed view. Therefore, although the three mountains are not very high, they are quite eye-catching. De County (formerly Dezhou) controls the intersection of the Tianjin-Pukou Railway and the Grand Canal. It is an important location bordering Shandong and Hebei. It has the convenience of vehicles and boats, and its commerce is thriving, serving as a major distribution center for soybeans and cotton. When the train entered the station, a military officer saw his family off on the train. According to what he said, when the rumors of North China's autonomy began to spread, this place feared that it would be taken advantage of by villains. He had paid extra attention to the issue of public safety. At the Lao Jun Tang in Sangyuan Town, north of the county, there are four ancient pine trees, with old trunks reaching the sky and green shade covering the ground, with a large iron bell hanging on one. It has a very ancient origin, said to have been carried by the Yellow River flood and suspended on the tree from afar. As the river channel has constantly shifted, such as during the reigns of King Ding of Zhou and Emperor Renzong of Song, it twice reached Tianjin to enter the sea north of the present-day Grand Canal. The Sangyuan area would be the first to bear the brunt, and the disaster of being submerged may have been even worse than the current disaster area of the breach. Therefore, the ancients implied the hanging of the bell, hoping that later generations would put their hearts into controlling the water and preventing disasters. It should not be dismissed as mere provincial chatter. After the train passes Sangyuan, it enters the border of Hebei in Cang County (Cangzhou, Changlu, all former names). The vicinity is the main production area of Hebei straw hats and whips, and the salt production is abundant, which is the Changlu salt that the world refers to. Then arriving in Tianjin, I got off the train to visit friends, and lingered for a while. Then I went to Beiping. Along the way, the plains are full of fertile wheat fields, the trees along the ridges are withering, but the sparse branches are everywhere. In the evening, as I was about to reach the old capital, I suddenly saw a fire in a residential building in the eastern suburbs, with the light shining on the city tower, fearfully burning. A gentleman in the same car, a military man from Shandong, was summoned by a fellow villager to come to Beiping to take up a job. Seeing the fire, he exclaimed with surprise, calling it a good omen for the future, and everyone around him chuckled. The markets in Beiping and Tianjin both seemed to have some anticipation due to the potential support from all sides. Therefore, after a period of turbulence, they have temporarily recovered and are in a state of harmony. However, it is impossible to predict whether this kind of superficial stability can last.

A Glimpse of Wuhu's Commercial Situation: Various Industries Turned Active Last Year, with Higher Overall Profits After Year-End Closing 70

Wuhu Correspondence: Wuhu is located in the middle reaches of the Yangtze River. Since the completion of the Jiangnan Railway and the Jingwu Highway, both water and land transportation have become more convenient. However, the commercial market still relies on the prosperity of the rice market. Since the great flood of the twentieth year, the rice market has plummeted, and various industries have been extremely exhausted. As a result, the social economy and people's lives have all fallen into a state of difficulty. Since last summer, through the efforts of officials and civilians to prevent floods, we have passed through dangerous passes. The autumn harvest was abundant, and the rice market has slightly recovered. After the Mid-Autumn Festival, the commercial market has shown signs of vitality. When the Italo-Ethiopian War broke out, the prices of foreign goods rose. The more inventory one had, the more profit one gained. At the end of the year, many had profits, and few had losses. This is a rare phenomenon in recent years. The following is an investigation into the general situation of important businesses last year.

Banks: There are seven banks in Wuhu: Central, China, Communications, Industrial, Shanghai, Farmers, and Anhui Local Bank. Since the elimination of money shops, the banking industry has controlled the financial hub and has been thriving. In addition, most of the transactions they engage in are collateralized loans, without the worry of bad debts, so they all have profits. The China and Communications banks can be regarded as the largest. As for money shops, only seven large and small ones remain. Their business volume is less than one or two-tenths of what it used to be. Yuankang has earned more profits by dealing in grain. Houfeng and others are just mediocre. Chengyu, which has enjoyed a long-standing reputation, has been greatly affected because a runner named Zhang embezzled millions of gold. It has not yet been decided whether it will continue to operate this year.

Rice Industry: The Wuhu rice market is the largest in Anhui. It is divided into the four major factions of Guangdong, Chaozhou, Yantai, and Ningbo, specializing in procurement and transportation. In addition, there are more than 200 rice mills, flour mills, and rice shops. Last year, the Chaozhou faction had the most business. Ruifa, Tongxin, Changfa, Tai Lee, and other firms all earned considerable profits. The Guangdong faction did not deal in any rice. Yuanchangxing, Yongchangli, and others only dealt in soybean transactions, making slight profits. Fuhua, Yuansheng, Dongfengsheng, and other firms in the Yantai faction also made slight profits. Business was sparse for the Ningbo faction. It is rumored that Yongfenggong will close this spring.

Cloth Industry: There are more than 40 firms in the cloth industry that have joined the guild. In recent years, threatened by economic recession, coupled with the loosening of goods prices, they have suffered uncompensated losses. After autumn, due to the abundant harvest in rural areas, business has become slightly more active. They compete with each other, offering discounts and prizes to attract customers. Also, with the prices of goods soaring, they have gained considerable profits. Dacheng can be regarded as the leader in the retail market. Firms like Qiru, Qixing, Guangda, Changrenji, and Hongzhang have also had profits. Wholesale transactions are larger than retail transactions, so Junyixiang has made a profit of more than 50,000 gold. Huxiangfa also has more than 20,000 yuan. Others, such as Changshun and Tianxiang, although they have reduced their scale, have also earned 2,000 to 3,000 gold. Guangxiang will close or reorganize this spring due to differences among shareholders.

Sundries: There are more than 100 sundries shops. In recent years, those engaged in wholesale have been cautious in extending credit, so on average, they are considered stable. Business was poor in the first half of the year, and inventory could not profit. In the second half of the year, there was a sudden turnaround, and the prices of oil and sugar soared again. Tung oil rose from 32 or 33 yuan to 60 or 70 yuan, and the thickness of the profits can be imagined. Hongda, Sheng, Tongsheng, Zaishengji, Yeyueji, and others have made the most profit. However, Shan Ruifeng, a firm with decades of history, has suddenly become immobile due to excessive losses over the years and has been stranded in invisible ways, with debts of more than 120,000 yuan. Although Shan Xingwu, a shareholder of the firm, has abundant assets, it is estimated that the distribution of debts will not exceed 20%.

Cotton Yarn: Cotton yarn transactions require huge capital, so statistics show that there are only a dozen cotton yarn shops in Wuhu. However, they are very united. They all gather at the guild every evening to discuss business policies, so the market price is consistent and there is never a case of indiscriminate sales. Over the years, they have all had profits and no losses for this reason. Last year, Tongchun, Baoyu, Cuishi, and Heng made the most profit. As for the only Yuzhong Textile Factory, it has suspended operations and is in liquidation due to debts of several million. The dispute over the dismissal of workers has recently been settled. (27th)

Jiangxi Province: Commercial Situation of the Past Year – Various Industries Are in Decline and Contraction 71

Nanchang Correspondence: Jiangxi's commerce last year, on the whole, was in a state of depression and contraction that had not been seen since the fifteenth year of the Republic. The economic panic and the difficulties faced by both the upper and lower classes were unprecedented. As a result, all industries had losses and no profits, and the future is quite bleak. The following is an investigation into the situation of various industries.

Jiangxi's commerce, in terms of exports, has plummeted in recent years. Even considering the six major special products, porcelain, ramie cloth, tea, paper, bamboo and wood, and rice, all are decreasing day by day. Eggs are a rural byproduct, and exporters of these were also losing money. Nanchang's commerce, affected by banditry, has seen a sharp fall because residents have no purchasing power. Silk fabrics, Beijing pastries, cloth, food, and other major industries, regardless of the size of the store, see few customers. The once-burgeoning travel agencies, restaurants, and military supply businesses have all been unable to sustain themselves after the departure of the large army suppressing the bandits. The money industry, the foremost of all industries, is facing the image of closure because depositors are wary, bad debts are increasing, and there is no profit to be made after the currency system reform. In the future, it is feared that only those with larger capital can make unexpected profits from lending, and the rest will be eliminated. The banking industry will dominate. Wholesale outside the county, due to the aftermath of banditry, has not recovered its vitality. Farmers are unable to make a living, and grain prices are lower than everything else. In the past, large wholesale goods in Nanchang, such as homespun cloth, white sugar, and handicrafts, are now not in demand. Either the outside counties have not recovered, or the floods are too deep, or the low grain prices hurt the farmers, and there is no commerce to speak of. From the above, Jiangxi's commerce is on the verge of total collapse. The only ones who have made a slight profit are a small number of rice, flour, and noodles.

In the past year, no less than hundreds of shops, large and small, have gone bankrupt. It is said that after the Lantern Festival, many will still be unable to open their doors. Because stores have always been outwardly strong but inwardly weak, a common problem. Medium-sized and large stores spend 300 to 1,000 yuan per month. Under the current low social purchasing power, daily sales, even if they do not require capital, are not enough to cope. Therefore, major stores are showing signs of financial strain, and downsizing, austerity, and rent reduction have become the consistent demands of all stores. Seeking cash and not offering credit or loans has also become a consistent and unwavering principle. (26th)

Han Fuju Appoints Cao Fulin to Suppress Liu's Bandits; Cao Immediately Leads Heavy Troops to Western Shandong; Liu's Bandits Have Already Reached Henan 72

Jinan Correspondence: Liu Guitang, the well-known and fierce bandit of southern Shandong, has recently gathered one to two thousand bandits in Hebei Province, intending to disturb Shandong. He has entered Henan from Hebei and has the potential to cross the Yellow River southward. Han Fuju, upon receiving the report, had previously issued orders to the troops and militias stationed in the areas of northern and western Shandong to take strict precautions. According to reports, Liu's bandits have reached the area of Wuzhi in Henan and are being jointly suppressed by the troops stationed in Hebei and Henan provinces. Therefore, Han convened the Chief of Staff of the General Headquarters, Liu Shuxiang, the Commander of the 29th Division, Cao Fulin, the Commander of the 74th Division, Li Hanzhang, and others at the provincial government at 3:00 PM on the 26th to discuss measures to prevent and suppress Liu's bandits. It was decided to appoint Cao Fulin, Commander of the 29th Division, as the general commander in charge of preventing and suppressing Liu's bandits, leading his subordinate units, the 86th Brigade commanded by Chen Dexin, and the 87th Brigade commanded by Rong Guangxing, to the area of western Shandong to prevent and suppress the bandits. In addition to those originally stationed in western Shandong, all of Cao's units stationed in Jinan have departed. Cao himself has also prepared to leave Jinan on the 28th, first going to the border of western Shandong and opportunistically intercepting them outside the province in order to resolve the issue of Liu's bandits as soon as possible. (26th)

Songjiang: A Review of the Commercial Market Amidst the Slump 73

The commercial situation in this county last year was far inferior to what it used to be, and the root cause lies in the lack of economic resources and the difficulty of circulation. Therefore, the most successful year-end collections only reached 70%, and some were less than 40%. If there had not been ample reserves in the past, it would have been difficult to maintain operations. A gloomy atmosphere enveloped the entire county. On the day that is traditionally held to welcome the God of Wealth, the Sen Tai Coal Shop in Zherunqiao closed down with a loss of more than 100,000 yuan, and more than 130 creditors became bankrupt. There were some dealings with various financial institutions, and the most substantial deposit belonged to Wang Zidong, an employee of the Chamber of Commerce, amounting to nearly 10,000. It is now estimated that the actual amount collected, considering the inventory, accounts receivable, and other factors, is unlikely to reach 10,000 yuan. Both parties are currently mediating. Zhengda Silk Shop has merged with Yida Silk Shop due to reduced business. Silk and other items are mostly luxury goods. The rice industry has seen declining rice prices, which has led to no profits for the industry. There are also some who are unwilling to continue and prefer to close down, probably several shops. However, this is still being remedied, so it has not been announced. The financial industry, including Xinyu Money Shop, pawnshops, banks, livestock money shops, and Chengda Money Shop, has seen profits due to stable operations, ranging from more than 40,000 to 10,000 gold. Zhang Yida Fan Shop, a century-old store, and Maxiechang Sundries Shop in the city have both decided to close.

Wuxi: The Truth About the Profits and Losses of the Rice and Money Industries 74

In the past few years, the money shop industry in my county has been affected by the slump in the silk industry, and has suffered huge losses from lending or pledging silk cocoons. Therefore, many have gone bankrupt. In recent years, with various banks engaged in lending, the scope of money shop operations has shrunk. Last year, Ruichangrun, Fuchangsheng, Defeng, Yuanfeng, Yonghengfeng, Fuyu, Zengda, Fuyuan, Shenyu, and other nine firms all adopted prudent policies and were able to make profits. Yonghengfeng was the best, with profits of more than 10,000 yuan. Defeng, Yuanfeng, and Shenyu each had profits of 3,000 to 5,000 yuan. However, Fuchangsheng, due to the impact of bad debts from lending in previous years, the shareholders Wang Yaochen, Wang Yuqing, Xue Shentian, Yang Hanxi, and others, had no intention of operating, and decided to close down at the end of the old calendar year to collect debts. Ruichangjian Silver Shop and Fuyuan Zhuang also had no intention of operating and decided to collect debts and liquidate. Baofeng, Jufeng, and Shenghe, three rice shops in Fengtang, also announced their closure and liquidation due to losses in last year's rice market. Yuansheng, Fuxin in Sanliqiao, and Yongshun rice shops in Beizhakou are also reorganizing internally and temporarily suspending operations. Zou Chengtai, Yixin, and Fuxin, three rice mills in Jiangjianshang, are not doing well internally and will temporarily shut down their machines during the first month of the old calendar year. They are currently trying to improve and will open their machines and operate as usual in February.

Three Native Banks Announce Closure 75

The native banking industry in Wuxi has always been the hub of various businesses, with as many as eighteen banks in the entire county. Since the January 28th Incident (1932), it has been affected by the decline of the rural economy and the pressure from the modern banking industry. Furthermore, the failure of silk factories has caused significant losses for the banks. Consequently, larger banks such as Bao Kang Run, Yong Ji Run, and Rui Yu have successively closed down. By last year, only eight banks including Rui Chang Run remained. After the autumn, one more bank, Zeng Da, was opened, but all banks were operating with tightened scopes and increased caution. In this year's major closure, most banks were still able to make a slight profit, with Yong Heng Feng being the best, estimating a net profit of over ten thousand yuan. However, Fu Chang Sheng, Fu Yuan, and Rui Chang Run Bank, due to too many bad debts, have no intention of continuing business and have decided to collect debts and liquidate. Yesterday, the banks that opened for business were Yong Heng Feng, Shen Yu, Fu Yu, De Feng, Yuan Feng, and Zeng Da.

Changzhou Sends Telegram Requesting Copper Coins to be Minted with Central Holes 76

The Wuyi Industrial Association believes that the purpose of currency is to facilitate the people, enabling swift transportation and easy inspection. After researching ancient texts, they found that coins used to have holes, hence the term "hole money" and "a string of a thousand coins." The hole in the coin was for the convenience of the people. Since the Guangxu era of the Qing Dynasty, silver and copper coins have been minted without holes. Comparing the two, silver coins without holes, because of their higher value and smaller quantity, can be wrapped and inspected without causing inconvenience to the public. However, copper coins without holes, despite being cheap and numerous, still need to be wrapped in paper. Inspecting private coins and accurately counting them inevitably requires unwrapping and re-wrapping, which wastes paper and time, causing great inconvenience. Recently, the association read in the newspaper that the Ministry of Finance is starting to mint new decimal subsidiary coins. Therefore, the executive committee resolved to send a telegram to the Ministry of Finance, requesting that the newly minted one-cent and half-cent copper coins be minted with central holes. Yesterday, the telegram was sent to various departments for review and compliance.

Yangzhou Grain Collection Incident Involving a Prostitute 77

Zhang Jinghu, a resident of Zhongxiao Street in the city, forged receipts at the county government's grain depot a few days ago, embezzling over eight thousand yuan of grain funds from rural villagers. Later, a villager presented the receipt to the depot to exchange for cash, and the forgery was discovered. It was immediately traced back to Zhang. Subsequently, County Magistrate Shan Ma ordered the police to arrest Zhang at the home of a prostitute named Yidianhong at No. 8 Shewei Lane in the Dizang Temple in the city. Zhang was placed in shackles and paraded through the streets. Yesterday, the county government sent police to arrest the prostitute Yidianhong, and she was interrogated by Shen Youchen, the director of land taxes. As a result, it was determined that during the current period of prostitution ban, the prostitute should not have allowed guests to stay overnight. Moreover, Zhang admitted that he had spent over forty yuan of the embezzled grain funds at the prostitute's house. Therefore, it was deemed necessary to punish the prostitute, and she was immediately detained and sent to the court along with Zhang Jinghu for handling.

Aftermath of the Jinsha Town Tragedy in Nantong 78

Luo Jingqing, a shareholder of Jinsha Town, distributed relief to the poor during the Lunar New Year. Due to the large number of people, the wall collapsed, killing thirteen people. The Nantong District Court prosecutor has confirmed the identities of the deceased. There were four men: Qiu Jinshuo, Zhang Jinhe, Zhang Wenjin, and Luo Shuihou; five women: Jiang Zhangshi, Xu Qinshi, Gu Qinzhen, Jiang Qiushi, and Jiang Qiaohou; and four children: Yi Zipei, Qiu Hailin, Jiang Shuihou, and Jiang Huanlian. Luo's family provided compensation for the funeral expenses.

Accident Involving a Xinchang-Haoba Bus in Hangzhou 79

The Xinchang-Haoba bus operated by the Haoxin Commercial Bus Company departed from Xinchang at 9:15 AM on the 27th. While traveling on a hillside about two miles from the Epu Station, the bus ran out of engine oil and could not continue uphill. The driver, Wang Deren, reversed the bus, but unfortunately, it fell into a field from a hillside over ten feet high. The bus was completely destroyed. Among the twenty-five or twenty-six passengers, two elderly women died on the spot, and over ten were seriously injured, with the rest suffering minor injuries. It was not until noon that a Westerner's car passed by and, upon seeing the situation, the occupants helped rescue the injured. They sent Zhang Pengnian, the third section chief of the Zhejiang Education Department, who suffered minor injuries, to the Sanjie Station to report the incident and dispatched another car to send the remaining injured to Zhixiang Hospital in Sheng County for treatment. Mr. Zhang arrived in Hangzhou last night for medical attention.

The Unification of Chinese Geography 80

— Professor Zhang Qiyun, China University

Since the founding of the Republic of China, Chinese geography has made significant progress, with many novel and gratifying achievements. The contributions from various aspects share a common theme: they all prove that our motherland is located on a complete continent and maintains a unified form. Today, our support for national sovereignty and opposition to territorial division is not only a great emotion of national consciousness but also a natural conclusion of academic research. Now, let's take a look at the main facts in human geography, biogeography, and geomorphology to illustrate this point.

From the perspective of human geography, the Chinese language is unified. Although various dialects exist in China, the grammar of each dialect, in terms of sentence structure, is almost the same throughout the country. For example, in Mandarin and Wu dialects, "Where are you going?" is "你到那裹去"? (Nǐ dào nà lǐ qù?). In Fujian and Guangdong dialects, it's "你去那裹"? (Nǐ qù nà lǐ?). Such small differences are already exceptions. Mr. Zhao Yuanren said, "Talking about the grammar of Chinese dialects is almost like talking about auxiliary particles." (Note 1) Chinese dialects use auxiliary particles to express the tone and attitude of certainty or doubt, and the usage varies from place to place, which is very complex. However, classical Chinese has a nationally consistent nature, and the auxiliary particles have changed very little historically. For more than three thousand years, the national language has been a natural force for uniting the Chinese nation. Not only have the sentiments of the ancients been passed down to future generations, but it also serves to maintain the hearts of the Chinese people throughout the country. The national language referred to here, of course, refers to both classical Chinese and the literary form of the national language.

The Han ethnic group is the foundation of the Chinese nation. The Han ethnic group is a cultural term, encompassing the large ethnic groups that have been assimilated since the beginning of history. Currently, there are still some non-Han ethnic groups in the border provinces, who speak non-Chinese languages, have lower cultures, and have not learned the national language. However, whether Chinese or non-Chinese languages, they all belong to the same language system. Centered on mainland China, extending south to the Malay Peninsula, west including Tibet and Myanmar, crossing the sea east to Taiwan, and north across the Shaan area to the upper reaches of the Yenisei River in Siberia, the languages spoken by the people in this region all belong to the monosyllable language family. Among them, they are roughly divided into four systems: Chinese, Siamese-Thai, Tibetan, and Burmese. If further combined, Chinese is related to Siamese-Thai, and Tibetan is close to Burmese. Linguists call it the Sino-Tibetan language family (Thai-Chinese, Tibeto-Burmese), or simply the Sino-Tibetan family. For example, the Yi (also known as Lolo) language is a branch of the Tibetan-Burmese language. According to Mr. Ding Wenjiang's research, the Yi script has the same origin as Chinese characters. For example, the first-person pronoun is Ma, and the word for tribe is Pu, which are the same in both Chinese and Yi languages to this day (Note 2). The Sino-Tibetan language family, also known as the Zhen-Qie language family, is the Chinese language family, and it has the following three characteristics: one character, one sound, that is, the so-called monosyllable; no word ending changes, the so-called isolating language; and the distinction between the four tones (level, rising, departing, and entering). These three characteristics are all possessed by the Chinese language family. The Japanese language, on the other hand, belongs to the agglutinative language family. Many auxiliary particles must be added between words to form the meaning of the whole, which is different from the Chinese language.

The excavation of the Yin Ruins in Anyang has been a major event in Chinese academia in recent years, and the underground historical materials obtained are extremely valuable. According to Mr. Li Ji's report, the tin content in the bronzes of the late Shang Dynasty was mostly above 10%, which had already reached the Bronze Age. The raw materials for copper and tin mostly relied on supply from the south. Oracle bone inscriptions not only contain the character for wheat but also the character for rice. The excavated animal bones contain the remains of water buffalo, and rice and water buffalo are both southern components. At that time, marine shellfish were also used as currency. Mr. Li said that the Yin people were able to mine gold from the southern country, capture whales in the East Sea, hunt in the north and south of the great river, and engage in conquests, writing, rites, and music. There was no one in East Asia who could compete with them, which was not a coincidence (Note 3). It can be seen that the reason why China is great lies in its ability to integrate the strengths of the north and the south from the beginning. Furthermore, Mr. Wang Guowei's research on the place names in the oracle bone inscriptions concluded that the area between Laiyi and present-day Hebei Province was still the territory of the Shang Dynasty, and its system and culture were completely the same as those of the Shang Dynasty. Observing the fiefdom of Jizi in the early Zhou Dynasty and the mandate of King Cheng to Sushen, it is known that the reputation of the Shang Dynasty extended far to the northeast (Note 4). The three major peninsulas of East Asia, the Shandong Peninsula, the Liaodong Peninsula, and the Korean Peninsula, were already one family three thousand years ago. Both old historical materials on paper and new historical materials underground can prove this undoubtedly.

Chinese plants, like the Chinese nation, are exceptionally rich in content, resulting from the convergence of species from many plant regions. There are Siberian elements in northern China, Himalayan elements in western China, and Malay Peninsula elements in southern China. China was originally a vast continent, without an ocean to separate it, so the elements of each plant region could be mixed with each other. Northern species are often distributed in the southern provinces, and southern species can sometimes be distributed in higher latitudes (Note 5). Because of the large number of plant species and the excellent soil and climate, economic plants are exceptionally prosperous. Grains, fruits, industrial plants, and flowers mostly originated in China. Many of the ornamental plants in European gardens are derived from China. Our country's plants are not only of scientific interest but also of special economic value. Take soybeans as an example. Currently, the soybeans on the world market are almost entirely exported from the three northeastern provinces of China. Soybean cultivation in the inland provinces can be considered for self-sufficiency, while farmers outside the customs (关外) mainly aim for export. Soybeans are also known as yellow beans, and the Western name is Soybean. Soy is the "菽" (shū) in "菽豆" (shúdòu, soybeans). The Guangya says: "大豆，菽也" (Dàdòu, shū yě - Soybean is shū). The character "菽" (shū) was originally used as a variant of "大豆" (dàdòu, soybeans), but now it has become a common term in the world. Our country has cultivated soybeans very early. The Zuozhuan records the distinction between soybeans and wheat, and Liu An invented tofu, all of which are well-documented. Tofu has been called the national dish by some. In addition, soy milk, bean sprouts, soy oil, bean cakes, soy sauce, and other products have been invented over the generations and are all modified products of soybeans. If we want to point out a domestic product to represent China's natural wealth, it must first be prevalent throughout the country, so that it can be seen in the cold north of the Great Wall and the heat of the Lingnan area. Second, it must be circulated among the people, so that even the isolated and ignorant in the Three Family Village (三家村) can have the value of not forgetting it with every meal. Third, it must have world significance or international reputation. Then, the world-famous soybeans of the three northeastern provinces are the best symbol of the geographical unity of China.

In recent years, there has been a major discovery in the field of geomorphology, which is the Yanshanian orogeny discovered by Mr. Weng Wenhao. The mountain ranges on the earth's crust each have their own generation, era and history. From the results of geological research in Europe, the orogenic eras usually recognized are several, with the Caledonian in the middle of the Mesozoic Era, the Hercynian at the end of the Paleozoic Era, and the Alpine in the middle of the Tertiary Period being the most important. European scholars believe that the formation of world mountain ranges is mostly limited to these three. For example, the Himalayan period in Asia is comparable to the Alpine period. Since the founding of the Republic of China, the Chinese geological community has made efforts to study the Chinese mountain ranges in detail, and only then did it realize that Chinese geology has its own special scale and does not need to be the same as others. The second half of the Mesozoic Era was the era when most of the orogeny and igneous rock activity in China were the most intense. It is too late to call it Hercynian, and it is too early to call it Himalayan. Mr. Weng summarized the results of years of investigation, inferred in detail, and created a new name for this major orogenic period, calling it the Yanshanian orogeny. This orogenic period had not been noticed on the Eurasian continent, and the initial evidence was mostly obtained from the Yanshan Mountains in Hebei Province. However, continuing research revealed that it affected areas from Jilin and Heilongjiang in the north to Yunnan and Guizhou in the south. In 1928, Mr. Weng read this paper at the Pacific Science Conference held in Tokyo, Japan. The papers were published in Science Magazine and the Geological Journal (Note 6). This point has reached a definite realm after repeated research. Thus, the so-called Yanshanian period has not only become the most important orogenic period in East Asia, but the Chinese continent as a whole structure has also been recognized by scholars around the world. After the Yanshanian movement, a large subsidence zone appeared in northern China, called the Bohai Inner Geosyncline. This is the predecessor of the current Bohai Sea. In ancient times, the Bohai Sea was much larger than it is now. It was only through the actions of nature, as if "Yugong Moved the Mountains" and "Jingwei Filled the Sea," that great alluvial plains were created around the Bohai Sea. These plains should all be included in the scope of the large inner geosyncline geologically. The Bohai Inner Geosyncline includes three parts: the Liao River Plain, the Bohai Sea itself, and the North China Plain. The so-called inside and outside the customs (关内关外) are not only closely related economically, but also a unit in terms of geomorphology. Also, the two major peninsulas of Liaodong and Shandong were originally connected, and the Dengzhou Strait was formed later. In the second half of the Cenozoic Era, faulting occurred on the Liaolu continent in the east, and the Dengzhou Strait appeared as a result. The intrusion of seawater formed the Bohai Sea. Although the two northeastern peninsulas are separated by the Dengzhou Strait, their geological structure and rock properties are very similar. In short, the Bohai Sea is entirely China's inland sea, and the land around the Bohai Sea is naturally China's territory. Any artificial boundaries violate natural form and obliterate national history. How can our people rest easy and how can we forget! (Note 1) See Zhao Yuanren's Research on Modern Wu Dialect, published by Tsinghua Research Institute in 1928. (Note 2) See Ding Wenjiang's Preface to the Literary Collection, published in the Journal of Geography, Volume 2, Issue 4, December 1935, published by the Chinese Geographical Society. (Note 3) See Li Ji's Report on Recent Excavations in Anyang and the General Account of Six Works, published in the Report on Excavations in Anyang, Issue 4, published by the Academia Sinica in 1933. (Note 4) See Wang Guowei's posthumous work, New Evidence of Ancient History, reprinting by Lai Ge in Beiping, 1935. (Note 5) See Marcel Hardy's World Phytogeography, translated and revised by Hu Xiansu, published by the Commercial Press, 1933. (Note 6) See Weng Wenhao's Mesozoic Orogeny in Eastern China, published in the Cone Finger Collection, issued by the Geological Survey in 1930.

Local News: Fourth Anniversary of the January 28th Incident - Citizens Hold Memorial Service - Ma Xiangbo and 18 Others Elected as Presidium - Over 800 People Sing Memorial Song with Solemn Enthusiasm - After the Meeting, the Entire Group Walks to Miaohang to Pay Respects at the Cemetery 81

According to Xinsheng News Agency, yesterday marked the fourth anniversary of the "January 28th" Incident. Various circles in this city, especially from the morning of yesterday at 9:00 AM, people from the city's industrial, commercial, academic, women's, and other circles, specially gathered at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce auditorium to hold a memorial service for the fourth anniversary. Over 800 representatives attended. Ma Xiangbo, Shi Liang, Shen Junru, He Xiangning, Zhang Naiqi, Zhou Jianyun, Yan Esheng, Wu Yaozong, Liao Maoru, Shen Zijiu, Liu Wang Liming, Wang Xiaolai, Zhang Yichen, Yang Weiyu, Jiang Wenyu, Luo Qinghua, Ouyang Yuqian, Li Gongpu, Hu Fengxiang, and 19 others were publicly elected as the presidium, with Yao Shou Kang as the master of ceremonies.

Chairman's Report

After performing the ceremony as usual, Shen Junru gave a report first. It was decided that the Youth Choir would lead in singing the "March of the Volunteers," which was solemn, enthusiastic, and sounded through the clouds. It was decided that Wang Zaoshi, Luo Qinghua, Li Gongpu, Shi Liang, and others would give speeches. The lengthy words are not recorded. Then, proposals were discussed.

Paying Respects at the Cemetery and Offering Flowers

At 12:40 PM, the 19 members of the presidium offered flowers and paid tribute in front of the Scout Memorial Stele at the City Chamber of Commerce. The remaining people from all walks of life were divided into rows of four and marched in an orderly manner, led by a white banner that said, "Shanghai Public Memorial to the Nameless Heroes of the January 28th Incident." Women were in the front, followed by men, passing through North Henan Road, Baoshan Road, West Baoxing Road, North Baoxing Road, Yuexiu Road, and directly reaching the Cemetery of Nameless Heroes in Miaohang. Along the way, they sang the January 28th song and the March of the Volunteers, which were solemn and enthusiastic. They arrived at the cemetery at 3:30 PM. The entire group stood in silence and bowed three times. First, the chairman offered flowers and read the memorial text. It was decided that Zhang Naiqi would report on the significance of the January 28th Incident. After the ceremony ended at 5:30 PM, the group marched back to Jiangwan Station in an orderly manner. It was already after 6:00 PM when they arrived, so they took the 6:30 PM Songhu train back to Shanghai.

Public Tribute to Xiao Te

The United National Salvation Association of various groups passed a resolution in the general meeting to appoint Tao Xingzhi, Yan Esheng, Li Gongpu, and Li's wife to represent the entire body in paying tribute to the tomb of the American Flying Colonel Xiao Te (Note: Xiao served our country in fighting the enemy and died in battle in the Soviet Union; he is buried in Hongqiao). However, due to the lack of time, the date was changed to today to go to the cemetery to offer flowers and pay tribute.

Memorial Text of the Assembly

The memorial text read: "The people of all circles in Shanghai, today with utmost sincerity pay tribute to the Tomb of Nameless Heroes, saying: We are willing to sacrifice our lives, property, and everything else from now on, and unite with the people of the whole country to complete the great cause of national liberation and repay the sacrifices of all the martyrs."

Half-Mast Flags Throughout the City

To commemorate the January 28th Incident, all agencies, groups, and schools throughout the city lowered their flags to half-mast as a sign of mourning. The Public Concession Police Department increased the number of detectives along the route to protect and guard against the public's march. After arriving in Zhabei, the Public Security Bureaus of the fifth and seventh districts also paid attention to maintaining order. The Municipal Security Department sent a company of soldiers from the second battalion of the first regiment to maintain order around the Tomb of Nameless Heroes in Miaohang.
