Delivery of January Government Bonds Must Be Made in Actual Bonds, No Futures Trading Allowed; Ministry of Finance Orders Stock Exchange to Comply and Dispatches Personnel to Verify Bonds Stored in the Three Banks 86

The Ministry of Finance, in view of the imminent delivery of January government bond transactions, in order to prevent the transfer or borrowing of bonds, facilitate the investigation of actual trading conditions, and prevent speculation and manipulation, issued an order on the 26th of this month to the Chinese Stock Exchange that all January government bond transactions must be delivered in actual bonds, and no futures trading is allowed. The Ministry also appointed Cheng Wujia, Zhao Fanlu, and Zhu Naipeng to visit the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications to jointly verify and seal up the bonds held by each bank under the headings of "Bond Preparation," "Deposit Preparation," and the bonds received for the issuance preparation of each bank. No unauthorized transfer of bonds is allowed without the approval of the Ministry. The original order is excerpted below:

Order to the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications:

The order to the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications states: "The Shanghai government bond market is currently rife with rumors, which have been thoroughly investigated by the Ministry. In order to prevent the transfer or borrowing of bonds and to investigate the actual trading situation, all bonds held by the three banks under the headings of 'Bond Preparation,' 'Deposit Preparation,' and the bonds received for the issuance preparation of each bank should be immediately sealed up and jointly verified by personnel dispatched by the Ministry. No unauthorized transfer of bonds is allowed without reporting to the Ministry for approval. Please comply accordingly (a corresponding letter is sent for your information and compliance)."

Order to the Chinese Stock Exchange:

The order to the Chinese Stock Exchange states: "The bond trading situation in the exchange recently and the occurrence of speculation and manipulation have been thoroughly investigated by the section chief of the Ministry and the supervisor of the Shanghai Exchange. In order to investigate the actual trading situation, all January government bond transactions must be delivered in actual bonds, and no futures trading is allowed. Please comply accordingly and report the delivery situation in detail for verification and handling. This order."

Their efforts in publicity and fundraising have been very successful. Over the years, they have donated over ten million yuan in relief funds. Recently, in light of the severe disaster situation in Northern Jiangsu, they have donated 40,000 yuan in national currency to the Shanghai Office of the China International Famine Relief Commission at 505 Henan Road in this city, to be used by the Yangtze River Basin Advisory Committee under its jurisdiction to support industrial relief. International Telecommunications Bureau Strives for International Calls; China-Japan Line Officially Implemented on February 15th; China-UK and China-India Lines Also Undergoing Testing 93

Since the International Telecommunications Bureau of the Ministry of Communications was taken over by Acting Director Bao Keyong, it has continued to actively test the China-Japan call project that was actively pursued by the previous Director Wen Yuqing, with the aim of officially launching the service as scheduled on February 15th. A reporter from the Central News Agency interviewed Tang Tiandong, the acting section chief of the Business Section of the Bureau, who stated:

China-Japan Line to Be Implemented as Scheduled

The China-Japan call project is currently still under testing. Tests are conducted every Monday and Thursday, and the results are satisfactory. The service can be launched as scheduled. As for the future call charges, the minimum call time is set at three minutes, costing 15 Japanese yen. Each additional minute will cost 5 Japanese yen. The reason for using Japanese yen as the standard is that international standards use gold francs, but converting to Chinese and Japanese currencies is troublesome. For convenience, Japanese yen is used as the unit.

China-UK Line Undergoing Testing

The International Telecommunications Bureau has previously tested call services with Italy, the Philippines, the United States, and Germany, with good results. However, due to insufficient radio station equipment, the services have not yet been officially launched. It is currently conducting call tests with the UK, also twice a week, but official launch is still pending.

China-India Line Revived

Due to the large amount of business between China and India, the Bureau previously proposed to India to establish direct calls between Shanghai and Mumbai to avoid the current hassle of relaying through Java. At the time, India did not agree. Recently, the other party suddenly brought up the matter again. It is currently planning to test the service, and it is hoped that it can be implemented in the shortest possible time.

Xu Qixing, Who Flew Around Europe, Sends a Letter of Thanks to the Aviation Association and Reports on the Aircraft Type and Flight Route 95

Xu Qixing, an overseas Chinese, previously flew his self-made aircraft around Europe, bringing honor to the country. The China Aviation Association sent a telegram to congratulate him and inquire about the aircraft type, engine, and flight route. The reply has been received, which is in English and translated by the association as follows:

Expressing Gratitude

I received your letter of the 6th of this month. I have just returned here from Daowa. I have just unloaded my luggage and am busy with worldly affairs. I apologize for the late reply. I am very grateful to the Shanghai China Aviation Association for its kindness and concern for my long-distance flight and for sending a telegram of congratulations. Please convey my thanks.

Aircraft Specifications

The aircraft used for this flight is the VV model. The details of the aircraft are as follows: The aircraft was designed by my friend Mr. Hu Laoyun. It is a low-wing monoplane with two seats side by side. The aircraft is made of wood. The leading edge of the wing is equipped with two British Bai Zuo Niagara engines. The stringers, small crossbones, and fuselage are all made by 美洲虎尾. It is covered with plywood. The landing gear is fixed and streamlined. The aircraft has a net weight of 650 kilograms and a full load weight of 1,100 kilograms. The maximum speed is 200 kilometers per hour, and the landing speed is 80 kilometers per hour (equipped with stall wings). With two engines, the flying altitude is 6,000 meters. With only one engine, the flying altitude is 1,800 meters. The aircraft is not equipped with wireless radio, only two blind flying instruments.

Flight Route: Starting from Batavia, via Singapore, Bangkok, Yangon, Calcutta, Allahabad, Jodhpur, Karachi, Chask, Bushehr, Baghdad, Aleppo, Adana, Istanbul, Budapest, Amsterdam, and finally London (Kraton).

Establishing a Factory in the Far East

The VV aircraft's round trip to Europe took 75.5 hours. The return trip took 72 hours. The average flying speed is about 200 kilometers per hour. Each engine has 90 horsepower. The range is 1,600 kilometers. The fuel consumption is 42 liters per hour, and the oil consumption is 1.5 liters per hour. I am currently a businessman, but I am researching and preparing to establish an aircraft manufacturing factory in the Far East to manufacture various types of military and commercial aircraft. Because I have had this goal for a long time, I undertook this long-distance flight to Europe.

Overseas Chinese Care About Their Motherland; Request for Establishment of a Shortwave Radio Station 96

According to the Zhong Shi News Agency, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission sent personnel abroad last year to investigate overseas Chinese affairs in Southeast Asia and Africa and to inspect local consulates. After returning to China, Commissioner Liang Yu and others learned that overseas Chinese in various places felt extremely disconnected from all the news about the political construction of their motherland in recent years. The love of the overseas Chinese for their motherland's National Day is unusually deep. They wanted to receive news from their motherland by radio, but China's Central Broadcasting Radio Station uses longwave broadcasting, making it difficult to reach places that are too far away. However, National Day propaganda is very important, not only in relation to the connection between the government and the overseas Chinese but also in terms of international impact. The Chinese government has no equivalent written propaganda in South Africa, and the Western newspapers there rarely publish news about China. As a result, patriotic overseas Chinese who care deeply about their motherland often feel depressed. Therefore, Liang drafted a memorandum, submitted it to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, and forwarded it to the central government, requesting the establishment of a shortwave radio station to benefit overseas Chinese. It is reported that after receiving a letter from the Central Secretariat, the Central Broadcasting Radio Station Management Office has begun preparations and has submitted a draft plan. Once approved by the National Government, it will gradually establish shortwave radio stations in various places in Southeast Asia and Africa.

Ministry of Finance Approves Chamber of Commerce's Request Regarding the Purity of Silver Used by Silversmiths 98

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce previously received a letter from the Silversmiths' Guild, requesting that it be forwarded to the Ministry of Finance, concerning the use of silver in the manufacture of silver ornaments and utensils by silversmiths. The guild requested that the old standards of silver content be maintained. The Chamber of Commerce submitted the request to the Ministry of Finance on November 25th of last year, and yesterday received a reply from the Ministry of Finance, document number 843 in the Finance Department, stating, "We have received your submission. The 'Regulations for the Management of Silver Used in Silver Products' promulgated by this Ministry were originally intended to preserve our country's silver reserves and maintain economic stability. Therefore, the regulations stipulate that chemical silver should be used as the raw material for silver products. If pure silver must be added, the amount of pure silver should not exceed 30% to show restriction. Moreover, the manufacture of silver utensils and ornaments is inherently extravagant. Currently, various European and American countries are switching to chemical silver as a substitute and plating it with gold and silver, which is inexpensive and of good quality. This practice can be imitated. We hereby extract the following compositions for your reference: 1. Nickel 10, Copper 45, Zinc 45; 2. Nickel 10, Copper 65, Zinc 25; 3. Nickel 12, Copper 62, Zinc 26; 4. Nickel 15, Copper 40, Zinc 45; 5. Nickel 15, Copper 50, Zinc 35; 6. Nickel 15, Copper 64, Zinc 21; 7. Nickel 18, Copper 58, Zinc 24; 8. Nickel 18, Copper 65, Zinc 17; 9. Nickel 20, Copper 55, Zinc 25; 10. Nickel 20, Copper 60, Zinc 20; 11. Nickel 20, Copper 75, Zinc 5; 12. Nickel 24, Copper 41, Zinc 35; 13. Nickel 25, Copper 50, Nickel 25; 14. Nickel 25, Copper 55, Nickel 20; 15. Nickel 30, Copper 47, Copper 23. Chemical silver, also known as nickel silver, is an alloy of nickel, copper, and zinc (sometimes with added tin, aluminum, lead, and iron). There are currently over 150 types sold in markets around the world. Our country's silver product industry is clinging to old ways and is already lagging behind. We should promote this type of alloy industry in order to save costs and benefit competition. The artistic effect is the same. If silver must be added, this Ministry has ordered the Central Mint to comply with Article 2 of the 'Regulations for the Management of Silver Used in Silver Products' and research alloy materials with a silver content of no more than 30%, combining silver, copper, nickel, zinc, and other substances. The Mint has prepared six types of such alloy materials, whose compositions are as follows: 1. Silver 30, Copper 50, Nickel 10, Zinc; 2. Silver 30, Copper 50, Nickel 6, Zinc 14; 3. Silver 25, Copper 50, Nickel 15, Zinc 10; 4. Silver 20, Copper 50, Nickel 20, Zinc 10; 5. Silver 30, Copper 60, Nickel 3, Zinc 7; 6. Silver 30, Copper 60, Nickel 5, Zinc 5. The above six types of alloy materials are white in color. Although the texture is slightly hard, it will not be difficult to process if heated and hammered, and they can be used to manufacture silver utensils and ornaments. In addition to this Ministry ordering the Central Mint to prepare and supply the above alloy materials, you must also comply with this Ministry's previous order that silver utensils and ornaments still be made using chemical silver as the raw material. If silver must be added, the above alloy materials should be used immediately, and the regulations should not be changed. As for your request to report the pure silver content of existing silver utensils and ornaments and the pure silver content of existing silver materials separately as two categories, silver utensils and ornaments and silver materials, this is feasible. In addition to distributing this notice, you must comply accordingly."

Page 14

Strange Tale of Ice Blocking Navigation Off Dagu Port; Sea Ice Extends 150 Li, A Rare Occurrence Since the Early Republic; Chinese Merchant Ships Have All Suspended Service 101

This year, North China has experienced severe cold, with the Baihe River freezing over. Even off Dagu Port, the sea surface has frozen for more than 100 li, blocking waterways and obstructing traffic. This is a rare cold snap not encountered since the early years of the Republic. Shanghai-based shipping lines have been affected, resulting in numerous accidents. Now, Chinese merchant ships have completely suspended service. Detailed information is provided below:

Baihe River Ice Blockage

The Baihe River in Tianjin is the only waterway from Tanggu to Zizhulin, and it is also the passage for North China ships entering and leaving Tianjin. This year, the Baihe River has frozen more severely than in previous years, impeding navigation. Earlier this month, the Tianjin Customs announced that the inner harbor of the Baihe River was covered with ice more than one foot thick, obstructing waterway traffic and making navigation dangerous. The Tianjin Customs issued a notice to all shipping companies nationwide, declaring that the Baihe River was icebound and that even icebreakers could not effectively lead ships in. Therefore, ordinary North China liners could only sail to Tanggu Port. This was the situation before the 10th of this month.

Sea Surface Freeze

The sea surface off Dagu Port is rarely affected by severe cold and freezing. After the 15th of this month, the climate in Tianjin underwent drastic changes, and the cold intensified. After the Baihe River froze, the sea surface off Dagu Port also began to freeze. After accumulating for many days, on the 16th and 17th, the ice layer extended from Dagu into the sea, reaching a length of 13 nautical miles. After the 18th, the ice field expanded daily and the ice layer thickened daily, stretching out in a continuous expanse, solidifying into an ice land. The frozen sea surface reached 45 nautical miles (over 140 li), with an ice thickness of over one foot. Not only could people walk on it, but also carriages and horses could gallop on it. Looking out, one could almost believe they were in the Arctic Circle. This unprecedented ice sea is the only one seen since the early years of the Republic.

Merchant Ships in Distress

This unprecedented freezing has created a great danger for the shipping industry in Tianjin. Before the 17th, merchant ships that braved the ice to enter Dagu Port were surrounded by heavy ice fields, unable to advance or retreat. The Xinshuntian, the first ship to be affected by the ice, had special icebreaking equipment and very thick steel, but it still broke its iron plates due to the impact of the ice. The Taishun of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and the Kunshan Maru of the Nisshin Kisen Kaisha endured countless hardships within the ice enclosure, sometimes ramming head-on, sometimes sweeping with the stern, advancing an inch and retreating a foot, and finally breaking through the encirclement after all kinds of dangers. As a result, the Taishun's hull was also damaged by the ice. At the same time, the number of other merchant ships that encountered danger is too numerous to mention.

Japanese Ship Aground

The Ekishin Maru, a cargo ship of the Dalian Kisen Kaisha's Shanghai-Tianjin liner service, has a cargo capacity of over 3,000 tons. This time, it was stranded by the solid ice, and its hull was grounded on the south shoal of Dagu Port. Because the ice is thick and difficult to move, it cannot be rescued. After the 18th, the Japanese ship was pushed onto the shoal by the ice floes. In less than three days, the ship was elevated so high that it resembled a multi-story building built on the beach. It is said that it will have to wait until the spring thaw before it can be rescued, at the earliest in two months.

Yushun Damaged

The Yushun of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company was heading to Tianjin this time, but it encountered ice before reaching Tanggu. It could not move forward or backward. The shipowner, Li Yunqu, struggled for several days, resulting in a shortage of coal and water. He telegraphed Shanghai for help, and finally managed to enter the port on the 23rd, but the front cargo hold had been damaged and was leaking water. After inspection by the Tianjin Customs, it was forbidden to sail. It must first be repaired and wait for an opportunity to follow another ship out of this ice enclosure before returning to Shanghai for repairs.

Chinese Ships Suspend Service

The Chinese merchant ships on the North China route in this port, which originally numbered over 20 and transported miscellaneous grains and coal, have now completely suspended service to Tianjin due to the ice field on the waterway and the obstruction of the route. They have switched to Longkou, Yantai, and other places. The Xinfeng of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's regular North China line has also been diverted to Yantai to transport salt, and the Xinming has been transferred to Fuzhou. Regular service will be resumed after the thaw. Only Taikoo and Jardine Matheson ships are still operating because they have icebreaking equipment, but their schedules cannot be guaranteed.

According to the Japanese-language Shanghai Nippo, the malignant influenza that is rampant in Japan has been quite severe since it began spreading last winter. Great-Grandson of Li Hongzhang Enters Vagrant Work Training Center; Li Daoqiang, Only 15 Years Old, Already Spends Money Like Water; Family Hopes He Will Reform and Forces Him to Learn Diligence for Three Years 106

According to the Datong News Agency, Li Daoqiang, the great-grandson of Li Hongzhang, the former Qing Dynasty grand secretary, is only 15 years old. Because he spends as much as 20,000 to 30,000 yuan every year, his family can no longer bear it and has sent him to the Caoxi Road Shanghai Vagrant Work Training Center to learn skills in order to reform his mind and body. A Datong News Agency reporter, upon receiving this news, drove to the center yesterday to inquire. The details are recorded as follows:

Young Age, But Addicted to Extravagance

Li's family fears that he will become addicted to extravagance and be unable to continue the family's legacy. Although Li Hongzhang's ancestral home was Hefei, Anhui, most of his descendants now reside in Shanghai. His great-grandson, Li Daoqiang, is only 15 years old. He studied at home with a tutor in his youth and recently transferred to the junior high school department of a certain middle school in Xujiahui. Although he is young, he is immersed in the extravagance of Shanghai, spending money like water and frequenting various gambling dens. It is estimated that he wastes as much as 20,000 to 30,000 yuan every year.

Sent to Work Training Center Hoping for Reform

In order to reform his mind and body, he was recently sent to the Caoxi Road Shanghai Vagrant Work Training Center, hoping he would repent. A Datong News Agency reporter drove to the center yesterday to inquire and met with the center's director, Mr. Wu, who did not deny the matter of Li Daoqiang being sent to the center for work training. According to him, according to the center's regulations, all those who enter the center for work training, regardless of whether their family is rich or poor, must work and learn diligence. However, since Li entered the center, he has still refused to work, so he must undergo a considerable period of guidance before being given work. Also, according to the center's regulations, those who enter the center must work diligently for three years before being allowed to leave. Therefore, the center will also handle Li according to the regulations and will not make an exception.

Family Asks to Refuse Visitors

The Datong News Agency reporter then asked Mr. Wu to introduce him to Li, but Mr. Wu politely refused, saying that he had been instructed by his family not to allow anyone to meet him, regardless of who they were. Subsequently, under Mr. Wu's guidance, the reporter was taken to visit various parts of the center. The internal facilities were completely modeled after a prison. There are currently over 800 vagrants, some working diligently and others attending classes. The discipline is extremely strict. Unfortunately, the reporter did not know Li's appearance, so he was unable to find and meet him.

Brief History and Current Situation of the Work Training Center

The Caoxi Road Shanghai Vagrant Work Training Center was jointly established in 1926 by Li Pingshu (deceased), the chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Council, and various public organizations. It began accepting vagrants in August 1929. The source of funding is an annual subsidy of 12,000 yuan from the Shanghai Chenghuang Miao Board of Directors, and the remainder is allocated by the Shanghai Charity Association. The entire center occupies 94 mu of land and is divided into adult and children's sections, each with dormitories, workshops, lecture halls, classrooms, dining halls, and hospitals. The sources of vagrants are: ① sent by the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau and the Public Security Bureau; ② recommended by organizations or individuals who donate more than 500 yuan annually; ③ recommended by the center's directors; ④ requested by the vagrant's family, but the cost of food and clothing must be borne by themselves, with a monthly fee of six yuan, which must be prepaid for three years upon entry. The vagrants in the center are paid for their work, with a minimum monthly income of two to three yuan and a maximum monthly income of six to seven yuan.

Seventy-Year-Old Man Sues Son; Shows Anger in Court; Rong Shangqian Sues to Revoke Eldest Son's Inheritance Rights; Eldest Son Pleads Guilty with a Rod in Court; Father's Anger Unresolved; - Debate on the Case Concludes; Judgment to be Pronounced Tomorrow - 107

Rong Shangqian, a seventy-year-old man from Guangdong who has retired to a villa in Jing'an, is in a bitter feud with his eldest son, Rong Peng. Rong Peng previously filed a lawsuit against Rong Shangqian in the name of his children's legal representative, seeking division of property. The third instance concluded, and Rong Peng appealed. Shangqian then hired a lawyer to invoke Article 1145 of the Civil Code and filed a lawsuit in the First Special District Local Court, requesting the revocation of Rong Peng's inheritance rights. A trial has already been opened, as reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Peng Shiye continued the hearing. Both the plaintiff and the defendant appeared in court. The plaintiff's second son, Rong Hong, also attended the hearing. Although the plaintiff is over seventy years old, his

Vigor Unabated

During his statement, he seemed to be furious. According to him, the defendant and his children were all educated by him. The defendant spent a lot of money studying in the United States. After returning, he still provided thousands of yuan annually. However, after his mother died, he plotted to kidnap him. Last year, he sued him. How can a son kidnap his father, or a son sue his father? He really couldn't bear it and filed a lawsuit to revoke his inheritance rights. Judge Peng then advised that these were all past events and did not need to be traced back, and that a father and son going to court was contrary to etiquette. If he wished to withdraw the lawsuit, the defendant should be ordered to provide a

Letter of Repentance

And be a dutiful son in the future, without any unfilial behavior. Upon hearing this, Rong Peng immediately expressed his willingness to comply with the court's good intentions and pleaded guilty to his father in court with a rod. However, Rong Shangqian still showed anger, patted his chest, and shook his head, saying that his son's previous accusations were all nonsense. After his mother died, she only left 10,000 yuan of property. The defendant initially claimed that there were 400,000 yuan of inheritance, and now he claims there are 2 million yuan. The judge asked him how much property he had now. The plaintiff replied that he had served in the government for forty years, so he had some property, several tens of thousands of yuan. In recent years, he has been doing business, and the profits are uncertain. He also owes people money. The judge then instructed him that since you

Do Not Want to Reconcile

And must deprive the defendant of his inheritance rights, then you should provide evidence and state the reasons. If you rely on your empty words, the defendant will also not be convinced. Thereupon, the plaintiff detailed his history of serving in the government during the late Qing Dynasty and early Republic to prove that the defendant's claim that he had not served in the government for long was untrue. The court then inquired about the current situation of the second son, Rong Hong, and the usual relationship between them. The plaintiff said that Hong was dutiful. The court continued to ask, "You have two sons. In the future, your estate should be inherited equally by both sons. Now you are requesting the revocation of your eldest son's inheritance rights. To whom will this share belong?" The plaintiff suddenly said, "It will be kept for

Food and Clothing

Expenses." The judge said, "Eating and clothing do not require that much. What do you mean?" The plaintiff shook his head and said nothing. The judge said, "If you want to file a lawsuit, according to the law, to lose inheritance rights, there must be two elements: insult and abuse. You don't need to be angry. You can speak calmly and in detail, and provide evidence for verification." The plaintiff was silent. The judge then ordered the lawyers of both parties to debate. The plaintiff's lawyer spoke first, saying that three or four years ago, during the Mid-Autumn Festival, the defendant presented pastries to his father. The plaintiff tasted a little, and the rest was given to the family. The abdomens of those who ate it later all swelled. This can certainly be called abuse, but now there is no evidence to prove it. However, the

Insult Aspect

Is a certain fact. Before the defendant and the plaintiff were involved in the lawsuit, the mediation statement submitted by the defendant was like a false accusation. It was an act of disrespecting elders. The statements in the document were mostly fabricated. Therefore, the plaintiff is requesting the revocation of the defendant's inheritance rights in accordance with the law. The defendant's lawyer then argued that the mediation statement in the previous case was written by lawyer Liu Shifang on behalf of the defendant. Because the letter the defendant sent to lawyer Liu at the time contained slanderous remarks, lawyer Liu was inevitably emotionally agitated, so he inadvertently revealed this in the mediation statement. This was not the defendant's own fault. Since the country allows people to file lawsuits, filing a lawsuit cannot be considered an insult. The judge then concluded and scheduled the judgment to be pronounced on the afternoon of the 3rd of this month.

Begging for Money from a Thief, Shocked to See a Pistol; Reported to the Police and Tracked Him Down; High School Janitor Rewarded for Reporting; Rickshaw Puller Injured by Stray Bullet and Sent to Hospital 108

Gao Xiaoguanzi, a man from Jiangbei, is 28 years old. He used to be a detective, but recently he has fallen into poverty and become a beggar. At around 3:00 AM yesterday morning, Gao was alone, waiting for pedestrians to pass by at the intersection of Longmen Road and Racecourse Road in the Public Concession, begging for copper coins. At that time, a pedestrian was walking west along Racecourse Road, turning into Longmen Road and walking south. Gao went forward to beg from him, but the man, seeing that a beggar was begging from him, became angry, pulled out a pistol, and threatened Gao, forbidding him to make a sound. Gao was shocked and stepped back a few steps, watching the man with the gun turn into SiDuYa Road and walk east. Gao knew that he must be a bandit robbing people, but he was frightened and unwilling to submit. So he followed him stealthily, intending to report to the police. However, there were no police officers in that area. He followed him to the front of the Great World Entertainment Center on the corner of MinTiNi Road, and saw the man turn south along MinTiNi Road. Gao saw Chinese Constable No. 408 of the French Police Station standing guard in front of the Great World. He went forward and reported to the constable, who tracked down and arrested the suspect. When they reached the entrance of the LaiCai Market Street (NingXing Street), the thief with the gun discovered that he was being chased by the police. He pulled out his pistol, fired backward to resist arrest, and turned into LaiCai Market Street, fleeing east. Along the way, he fired to resist, and a stray bullet grazed the left calf of Zheng XueLi, a rickshaw puller from Jiangbei who was resting by the roadside. Constable No. 408 immediately fired three shots in return and blew his whistle to summon police officers from nearby posts. The thief then turned into the west side of Xin Qiao Street and headed south. The beggar Gao XiaoGuanZi also helped to chase him. The patrol constables of the Fa Da Ma Road station, Chinese Constable No. 135 and Vietnamese Constable No. 341, heard the whistle and gunfire and rushed to the west side of Xin Qiao Street on Fa Da Ma Road to intercept the thief. Chinese Constable No. 135 also fired one shot to stop the thief from advancing. He captured the thief, seized a Brownling pistol, and found four live bullets in the gun. He then took the thief, the beggar Gao XiaoGuanZi who reported the incident, and the injured rickshaw puller Zheng XueLi to the police station. Under interrogation, the thief gave his name as Peng GaoSheng, 27 years old, from Pudong. He said that he had been a boatman but was now unemployed and had resorted to theft. The detectives searched him and found over ten yuan in banknotes and some silver coins. He was immediately sent to the Lu Jia Wan General Police Station. After questioning by the police chief, he ordered that the informant, Gao XiaoGuanZi, be rewarded with three yuan in legal tender and sent away. The rickshaw puller was rewarded with one yuan and sent to the hospital for treatment. The thief, Peng, was detained for investigation and sent to the court for trial.

Efforts Yield Results: Sunken "Yafu" Floats: Covered in Mud, Iron Completely Rusted 111

The Norwegian merchant ship "Yafu," which was sunk by the Chinese merchant ship "Tongde" in the waters off Lujiazui, Pudong, at 9:00 am on December 17th of the year before last, has been salvaged by the Russian Far East Salvage Company after repeatedly dispatching experts to oversee the work and spending over 100,000 yuan. Because the ship's hull was heavy, it suffered several setbacks. The Jianghai Customs Authority, considering the sunken ship an obstacle to navigation, had considered bombing it. However, the company did not show weakness and, in September of last year, added water pumps and floating cranes to continue the work. First, the masts and funnels were dismantled to facilitate the operation. After three months of work, the water in all the cabins was completely pumped out. Suddenly, at high tide on the day before yesterday evening, it automatically floated to the surface. The entire body was covered in mud, and the iron plates were completely rusted. It will then be towed into the dock for major repairs. As for the municipal ferries operating to the Chunjiang Wharf in Pudong and the Beijing Road Wharf in Puxi, which had previously changed to the South Customs Wharf in Pudong due to the salvage of the sunken ship, they will now return to the Chunjiang Wharf due to the floating of the sunken ship.

Yan Futang, a native of Shaoxing residing at No. 168, Yili, Rue Petain in the French Concession, is 55 years old this year and currently serves as the deputy manager of China United Trust Company (formerly known as Central, now renamed by the Ministry of Finance) on Beijing Road. Residents of Shengsi Island Oppose Division of Governance: Joint Petition to the Executive Yuan to Stop the Division Movement and Appeal to All Jiangsu Elders for Assistance 116

Since the Ningbo Shanghai Fellow Villagers Association petitioned the Executive Yuan to include the Shengsi Islands in Zhejiang Province's governance, various Jiangsu Province aquatic product agencies and fishery groups have repeatedly telegraphed their opposition. The Chongming County legal groups opposed it even more strongly and sent representatives to Beijing to petition. Yesterday, Xu Jinshan and Yang Youcai, the chiefs of various townships, towns, baojia, and more than 200 people on Shengsi Island, jointly petitioned the President of the Executive Yuan to stop the Zhejiang Province's division of governance movement to quell disputes. They also published a notice in the newspaper appealing to all Jiangsu elders and brothers for assistance. The original petition and notice are recorded below:

To the Executive Yuan Petition

The Shengsi Islands belong to Jiangsu territory and have always been governed by Jiangsu. For hundreds of years, there has been peace and tranquility. However, recently, because Jiangsu Province is working hard to rectify things, a few Zhejiang natives, who do not want to act in private, have had fantastic ideas and incited local gentry to blindly petition for division. The news has spread, and they are deeply indignant. The Shengsi Islands are located north of Jinshanwei and are independent islands that do not overlap with the Zhoushan Islands of Zhejiang Province. During the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty, they were once sold to the British by unscrupulous elements and subsequently occupied. After Jiangsu gentry Zhang Shen memorialized and requested the Qing court to negotiate the recovery, from the point of view of geography and history, it should undoubtedly be governed by Jiangsu. The various statements made by the Ningbo Shanghai Fellow Villagers Association are actually being incited by others to blindly petition with embellished words. The small number of unscrupulous people who insist on dividing the governance to Zhejiang are for two reasons:

1. "Restore Cuttlefish Cage Fishing": Fishermen in Shengquan Island use nets to catch cuttlefish. In the 19th year of the Republic of China, fishermen from Wen and Tai in Zhejiang Province manufactured and drove cages to invade the fishing grounds. At that time, cage fishing was harmful to the breeding of cuttlefish and hindered the livelihoods of the islanders. Fishermen and fishery groups from our various islands filed petitions to the Jiangsu Province to ban it. Fishermen in Zhejiang Province, unable to implement cage fishing in our Shengsi Islands, repeatedly thought about dividing the governance to Zhejiang Province, thinking it was a radical solution. Thus, there was the riot and fighting in the 21st year, the boundary delimitation meeting of the Ministry of Industry, and this renewed request. Their purpose of restoring cuttlefish cage fishing is clear.

2. "Open Gambling to Deceive Fishermen": The Shengsi Islands are an important fishing area in Jiangsu Province. Every fishing season, fishermen gather here. Most of the people from Zhejiang Province on the various islands are kind, but there are also many stubborn ones. Every time the fishing season begins, when the fishermen's pockets are full, they open gambling dens to deceive the fishermen, causing the fishermen's hard-earned money to be swept away, and some have no way to make a living and become thieves. How painful is this! Fortunately, Chongming County has set up districts to strictly prohibit this trend. Otherwise, the fishermen's livelihoods and local security will be unimaginable. However, these unscrupulous people rely on this for a living. Now that it is banned, it is tantamount to killing them, so they urgently seek to divide the governance to Zhejiang Province to act in private. In summary, the reasons why the Shengsi Islands cannot be divided into Zhejiang are so strong, and the motives for requesting division into Zhejiang are like this. If it unfortunately becomes a reality, the future is dangerous and unbearable to imagine. Jinshan and others either grew up here or have lived here for many years. The benefits and harms are the same, and the pain is deeply felt. We dare to jointly request your approval to quickly stop this division of governance movement to conform to popular sentiment and quell disputes. (Omitted below)

Original draft of the announcement:

To all Jiangsu elders and brothers: The Shengsi Islands have always been governed by Jiangsu. Administrative facilities are progressing, and it is appropriate to ban cuttlefish cage fishing and strictly prohibit unscrupulous people from gambling to protect the livelihoods of fishermen, which is particularly appreciated by our islanders. However, there are unscrupulous people who are inconvenient to act in private, blindly petitioning the authorities to divide the governance to Zhejiang. Losing their minds and acting like lunatics, it is particularly hateful. Our residents of Shengsi vow to oppose it. In addition to petitioning the Executive Yuan to quickly stop this division of governance movement to quell disputes, we ask all Jiangsu elders and brothers to uphold justice and provide assistance. It is hoped.

After the questioning, the official said, "Today, the plaintiffs and witnesses have not reported, so we will schedule another hearing." Ni Yueqiu was returned to custody.

Sculptor Zhang Chengjiang Returns to China from France 122

Sculptor Zhang Chengjiang, who studied in France, went to France in the 18th year of the Republic of China and entered the Paris National School of Fine Arts to specialize in sculpture. His works have been selected for various exhibitions such as the French National Salon, the Autumn Salon, and the Tuileries Salon, winning international acclaim. He has been there for more than six years. He returned to Shanghai from Siberia the day before yesterday. His works have also been transported by sea in five boxes. It is said that he has been hired by the Shanghai Academy of Fine Arts to serve as a sculpture professor. In addition to his artistic pursuits, Zhang is enthusiastic about social undertakings. During his stay in France, he served as a member of the executive committee of the Paris Chinese Students Association and a director of the Paris Chinese Bookstore and Newspaper Agency.

Taikoo's Tongzhou Steamer to Change Course to Ningbo, Renamed "New Beijing No. 1"; New Beijing to Become Wuhu Hulk 123

The British Taikoo Company's Ningbo route steamer "New Beijing" is aging, and the company has decided to decommission it. It has now been decided that from today, the "New Beijing" will be transferred to Wuhu as a hulk. The Shanghai-Ningbo route will be replaced by the "Tongzhou" steamer, which originally sailed the Tianjin route. The name "Tongzhou" will be abolished and changed to "New Beijing No. 1." It has been repaired and refurbished and will depart from Shanghai today on its first voyage to Ningbo. The "Tongzhou" steamer used to sail to North China and was one of the three regular Tianjin steamers. It has excellent passenger accommodations and a fast speed, and the vessel is better than the "New Beijing."

Western Paint Industry Association Holds Joint Meeting of Directors and Supervisors; Discusses and Sets New Market Prices 124

The Shanghai Western Paint Industry Association held a joint meeting of directors and supervisors at 4 p.m. yesterday to discuss and set new market prices for this year. More than ten people attended, including Ma Shangjie, Xi Rungeng, Qiu Hongsheng, and Qian Deqing. Ma Shangjie chaired the meeting and, after the formal opening ceremony, reported the purpose of the meeting. Then, the important matter of setting market prices was discussed. The following resolutions were made regarding the principles for setting prices: (A) Bleaching powder and sodium sulfide will be sold according to market prices. (B) Other general goods will be priced at market price plus 3% (no discounts). (C) All transactions must be cash. Regarding the extension of credit sales, a standard should be set. The resolution was as follows: If credit is extended for one month, the price will be increased by 1% based on the original target price; for two months, it will be increased by 2%. If credit is extended to dyeing factories with seasonal payments, it will be increased by 4% (total of 7%). Other cases will be handled similarly. For transactions with fellow traders, whether local or from other places, sales will be conducted at market prices (excluding indigo), with cash transactions. If payment is delayed, an additional 1% will be charged per month. All fellow traders must cease transactions with informal dyeing factories (i.e., those renting factory space). The above regulations regarding cash transactions will be implemented uniformly from January 28th of this year. After discussion, the resolutions were recorded and announced to all members. The previous market price resolutions are hereby announced for compliance by all fellow traders. Anyone found to be outwardly compliant but inwardly resistant, competing beyond market prices, or deliberately disrupting or obstructing business will be severely punished by the association upon report or discovery after investigation and confirmation. No leniency will be shown. This is a special announcement.

The 267th Inspection Report on the Issuance Reserve of Central Bank Convertible Notes states: "In accordance with Article 13 of the Central Bank Law, this committee is responsible for inspecting the number of convertible notes issued by the bank and the reserve funds. The 267th inspection was held on January 25, 1936, at the Issuance Bureau of the bank. The inspection results are reported as follows: (A) The total amount of convertible notes issued is 22,064,1090 silver dollars, including 19,990,01160 silver dollar notes and 20,739,930 auxiliary currency notes. The total amount of convertible note reserve funds is 22,064,1090 silver dollars, including 15,930,08210 silver dollars in cash reserve. This cash reserve includes 10,321,7090.51 silver dollars deposited in the bank's issuing headquarters, branches, and sub-branches, and 5,609,1119.49 silver dollars deposited with other banks. The guarantee reserve is equivalent to 61,332,880 silver dollars. (B) The total amount of customs gold convertible notes issued is 373,324.7 yuan. The total amount of customs gold convertible note reserve funds is 373,324.7 yuan. This reserve fund includes 7,351.95 taels of standard gold, priced at 5.0779 customs gold, equivalent to 373,324.7 yuan. According to Article 22 of the Central Bank Law, the cash reserve must be at least 60%, and the remainder must be guaranteed by legal collateral. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60%, and the guarantee reserve is within 40%, which is in compliance with the law. This is a special report. January 27, 1936. Chairman of the Supervisory Committee of the Central Bank: Li Fusun, Supervisors: Xie Mengjun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jiyi."

Shanghai's New Pharmaceutical Industry 135

— Edited by China Credit Information Service (Shanghai Industry and Commerce Overview, No. 11) (1) The Past and Present of the New Pharmaceutical Industry

New medicines, commonly known as Western medicines, were introduced to China from Europe and the United States along with Western medicine. Although there is no clear timeline for its rise and fall, it can be roughly divided into three periods. The initial period from the initial import to 1904; the competitive period from 1905 to 1929; and the transition period from 1930 to the present. The situation of each period will be described below.

Initial Period - After foreigners opened Shanghai as a commercial port in 1842 according to the Treaty of Nanjing, new medicines began to be imported at this time. Initially, only foreigners and foreign bridge residents used them, and the people who operated this business were all foreigners, such as the British Hospital (although named as a hospital, it was actually a pharmacy), Lao Deji Pharmacy, Watson's Yong, etc. The lower-level employees were all Chinese. Later, the Chinese gradually gained trust in new medicines because of their rapid and simple effects. Gu Songquan, a Chinese employee of the British Hospital, first raised funds to establish a Chinese and Western pharmacy on Fuzhou Road (the current site of Kaiming Bookstore) in 1904. This was the beginning of Chinese people operating the new pharmaceutical industry. At that time, because there were not many pharmacies, and only this pharmacy was operated by Chinese businessmen, the profit was very high. Therefore, Chinese employees of other foreign pharmacies also raised funds to establish pharmacies, such as Huaying, Central, Huamei, Zhongde, Zhongfa, Huayang, and Nanyang (not the current Huayang on Second Horse Road and Nanyang on Nanjing Road). During this period, although the number of new creations increased year by year, the original pharmacies were not affected, and they all had huge profits every year. The reasons were roughly the following four points: the number of purchasers increased year by year, and the increase exceeded the turnover of the new pharmacies created each year; the types of business were wider than they are now, such as dental equipment, cosmetics, and photographic materials, which all belonged to the scope of pharmacy business; there were very few pharmacies in the mainland, and users purchased directly from Shanghai; and foreigners allowed more favorable conditions for Chinese businessmen in order to broadly sell their products, and the profit added to the price of goods by each pharmacy was also higher than it is now.

Competitive Period - After 1905, pharmacies such as Jicheng and Dalu Wuzhou were established one after another, and small-scale pharmacies such as Huade and Liji grew like mushrooms after rain. Due to too many businesses, the turnover gradually decreased until the outbreak of the European War, when it began to recover. Because during the war, medicines from countries such as the United States and Japan continued to be imported, while the source of products from European and Western countries was cut off, and prices rose sharply. For example, carbolic acid, which originally sold for 75 cents per pound, rose to 14 yuan; phenacetin, which originally sold for 3 yuan per pound, rose to 60 yuan; and 20 oil, which rose from 50 cents to 1.5 yuan per pound. Lion Brand 606, due to lack of goods, the highest selling price was as high as 120 yuan per branch (originally sold for 4 yuan per branch). Those who had inventory all made multiple profits, but after the war, the color faded again, and each family adopted a small profit policy in order to sell more, and some even divided their attention to their own brand products. At that time, the more famous products of this brand were artificial blood (produced by Wuzhou Pharmacy), 606 ointment medicine (produced by Taihe Pharmacy), Rendan (produced by Zhongfa Pharmacy), Chicken Brand Bone Pain Dew (produced by Jihuatang Pharmacy), Jiukewan (produced by Tang Shiyi Pharmaceutical Factory), Bailingji (produced by Jiufu Company), and other six kinds.

Transition Period - After 1930, the sales volume did not increase significantly, and the scope of business shrank day by day. Photographic materials have been completely taken away by those who specialize in this business, and most of the cosmetics have been occupied by Guang Sheng Hang, Family Industrial Society, and other cosmetics merchants, while dental equipment is sold exclusively by the Dental Business Association, and very few people purchase from pharmacies. The competition among the industry is even more intense, and they compete to sell famous medicines at reduced prices as a means of attracting customers. For example, red tonic pills, Pareto, aspirin, creosote, Scott's cod liver oil, Qingdaowan, Douan's ointment, etc., are all sold at cost or even below cost. Later, the Shanghai New Pharmaceutical Industry Association dissuaded them and canceled the reduced price sales advertisements, but secret competition is still inevitable, making it difficult to obtain profits. Therefore, the new pharmaceutical industry, although people outside the industry do not know the details, people in the industry have long regarded it as a chicken rib. Until Jicheng Pharmacy stranded in front (closed on October 28, 1934 and reopened on January 28, 1935) and Huaying Pharmacy closed behind, the image of decline began to be seen. Both pharmacies were known for their strong strength in the industry. In recent years, the industry seems to have a tendency to believe in manufacturing. For example, New Asia Pharmaceutical Factory, which used to manufacture and sell Peacock toothpaste and other cosmetics, has been specializing in the manufacture of various injections since the "September 18th Incident." Xinyi Pharmaceutical Factory was originally founded by the German merchant Xinyi Pharmacy. Since 1930, it has been taken over by Chinese merchants, and its Vitamin C Baoming is quite popular. Wuzhou Pharmacy can use a large part of its funds for drug manufacturing. Zhongxi Pharmacy also has plans to organize the Minyi Pharmaceutical Factory. Other pharmaceutical factories such as Haibo and Kangle are all committed to imitation, and it seems that they have realized that relying solely on sales is not a long-term solution. (To be continued)

Experts Talk About Attending the World Games 139

Regarding the selection of various sports candidates for the World Games, the board of directors of the China National Sports Advancement Association has made a resolution. The reporter interviewed various experts to solicit opinions. They are recorded separately as follows.

Ma John Talks About Selection Criteria

Ma John said that the World Games preliminary selection is presided over by the National Sports Advancement Association. Whether centralized training will be conducted after the representatives are selected depends on the economic situation. Attending the World Games this time is hopeless to win the championship, but it is for sightseeing and polishing, so that Chinese athletes can benefit from the experience of others. Therefore, in addition to achievements, the selection criteria must also take into account the representatives' physical fitness, morality, and sports cultivation, so that they can continue to work hard and create superior records after returning home after the World Games, so that Chinese sports can make rapid progress, and it will not be in vain to attend the World Games this time. I (Ma himself) and Song Dong will lead the team back north on the first day of the month, while Yuan Lideng is scheduled to return to Tianjin tomorrow (29th).

Dong Shouyi Talks About Basketball Talents

According to Dong Shouyi and Song Junfu, the basketball selection feels that China is very balanced in terms of front, center, and guard talents, and the strength is good. As for the official representatives, it must be decided after several battles with the strong Westerners in the city. This selection is completely based on talent as the standard, and will not be based on the winning group. No matter how strong a certain group is, it is inevitable that there will be weaknesses. On the contrary, there may be outstanding talents in the losing group. Therefore, this time we will select outstanding players from each team first, and then add appropriate training to increase the overall effort. If the strength is set to be based on the winning team, it will be more resident. In the future World Games, it may not be a smear.

Li Huitang Talks About Football Selection

According to Li Huitang, the opinion on the selection of football candidates to participate in the World Games is that in order to save travel expenses and avoid long journeys, the preliminary election is not necessary. Because this selection is purely based on talent as the standard, according to my speculation, the sports authorities have long recognized the individual skills at the National Games. The quota of 20 representatives is set, and about half of them can be occupied by Hong Kong and Guangdong. There are many good players among overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia, and three or four people can also be obtained. The rest should be selected from East China and North China. After all the representatives are produced, my opinion is to gather in Hong Kong for training to increase cooperation. Before going abroad, come to Shanghai to compete for several games, and then compete with strong teams along the way to learn from each other. If we don't encounter strong enemies in the first game of the World Games in the future, we may be able to get more opportunities to play. If there are no special accidents at that time, I will be able to make the trip.

Recent News on the Compilation of Terminology by the National Institute for Compilation and Translation 146

The recent work on the compilation of terminology by the National Institute for Compilation and Translation is summarized below:

Psychology Terminology: The portion of general psychology terminology was compiled and printed in December of last year. Afterwards, it was sent to psychology experts and psychology departments or education colleges in various places to solicit opinions. Currently, revisions from Wang Jingxi, Tang Bohuang, Shen Youqian, Ai Wei, and Wang Zhen have been successively returned. All of them have detailed revisions. Recently, the institute also received a joint letter from psychology experts in Beiping, including Lu Zhizhang, Liu Tingfang, Sun Guohua, Zhou Xiangeng, Chen Li, Pan Yuan, Chen Xueping, Fan Jichang, Bao Zhili, Wang Zhengkui, Cheng Kejing, and Gao Wenyuan. They have made many comments on the review methods of the psychology terminology compiled by the institute.

Electrical Engineering Terminology: After the first draft was successively sent for review since December of last year, until recently, Nankai University has returned the general, power, and telecommunications sections; Hunan University has returned the general, power, telecommunications, and electrochemistry sections; and the Shanghai Telephone Bureau has returned the general and power sections.

Mechanical Engineering Terminology: The institute previously commissioned Kang Qinggui, a full-time compiler, to compile mechanical engineering terminology. As of now, more than 10,000 cards have been made. The method of compiling electrical engineering terminology is still followed. Each term is written on a card, arranged in alphabetical order of English, and the Chinese, French, German, and Japanese translations are collected as much as possible. This supplementary and sorting procedure is very complicated. The institute recently specially appointed Cao Qiang, an expert in mechanical engineering, to work with Kang Qinggui to speed up the work. After the first draft is completed, it is still planned to ask the Chinese Institute of Engineers to recommend experts to review it.

Psychopathology Terminology: It has been submitted to the Ministry of Education for instructions on publication.

Chemical Engineering Terminology: More than a month after the first draft of the first ten parts of the chemical engineering terminology was sent out by the institute, Zeng Zhaolun, Li Shouheng, Chen Tiaofu, and the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau have all completed their reviews and returned them. Regarding the candidates for the terminology review committee, the Chinese Chemical Engineering Society has appointed Wu Qinlie, Zhang Kezhong, Zhang Hongyuan, Jin Kaiying, Gu Yuzhen, and Xu Zong six people, and the China Chemical Industry Association has appointed Xu Fengshi, Chen Pingcheng, Zeng Guangfang, Zhang Zeyao, Xu Mingcai, and Cao Liangxia six people as representatives. After the representatives of the Chinese Chemical Society are appointed, they will be submitted to the ministry for additional appointment.

Vocational Education Society's Agricultural Tour: National Inspection Team Returns to Shanghai; Traveled Through Seven or Eight Provinces, Covering 20,000 Miles; Collected Extremely Rich Information Deep in the Countryside 148

The National Rural Inspection Team organized by the Agricultural Society of the Chinese Vocational Education Society, consisting of team members Xiang Shang, Yao Huizi, Wang Benren, Li Tao, and Zhong Tianshi, departed in March of last year, traveled through seven or eight provinces, covering tens of thousands of miles, and has now completed the inspection and returned to Shanghai yesterday. Details are as follows:

Traveled Through the Provinces of Guangdong, Guangxi, Guizhou, and Yunnan

The team of five departed from Shanghai on March 8 of last year. The purpose of this trip was to conduct on-site inspections of rural conditions in order to prepare for rural service work. They first went to Xiamen, Shantou, Hong Kong, and Guangzhou, then to Wuzhou, Guilin, and transferred to Kunming, Baise, and finally to Chengdu. Now they have returned to Shanghai via Chongqing, Yichang, and Hankou, traveling through the provinces of Fujian, Guangdong, Guangxi, Guizhou, Yunnan, Hubei, and Sichuan, covering approximately 20,000 miles, and lasting for a total of ten months.

Detailed and Thorough Inspections Along the Way

The purpose of this trip was to inspect, not to travel, so the inspections and investigations were very detailed wherever they went. They sought details on rural life, the conditions of the Miao people, border facilities, customs, diet, education, culture, etc. Therefore, the collected materials are extremely rich. Several times, due to venturing deep into the countryside, their lives were often in danger. Their courageous spirit is truly commendable.

Compiling Reports for Public Viewing

After returning to Shanghai the day before yesterday, the team stayed in the Chinese Vocational Education Society and began compiling inspection reports for public viewing. Two other team members have been hired by the Rural Department of the Bank of China in this city as instructors.

Children's Education Novel: Little Men (1)(6)(0) 158

— Original by Louisa Alcott, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang

"He has never borrowed a penny from me in his life," Moore exclaimed, looking quite alarmed, because he had thought of what was going to be said next, and generally speaking, he would rather someone was using witchcraft, because he greatly admired Don.

"Maybe he took it," said Ned, who couldn't help but hold a grudge after being immersed in water, and since he was no different from the average boy, he was willing to repay him.

"Oh, Don!" cried Ned, clasping his hands together, still holding a half-buttered piece of bread.

"This is a painful matter, but I have to clear it up, because I can't have you spying on each other like detectives, making the whole school so uneasy. Did you put that foreign coin in the warehouse this morning!" Mr. Pei asked.

Don looked straight at his face and replied without hesitation, "Yes, I put it in."

Then the sound of whispering arose from all around, Tomo's water bottle accidentally fell and shattered; little May cried, "I knew it wasn't Ned who took it;" Nan began to cry, and Mrs. Shu left the room, looking so disappointed, melancholy, and ashamed, that Don really felt uncomfortable. He covered his face with both hands, and then straightened up, shrugged his shoulders, as if to take up the burden, and then said with a stubborn face, half firm and half reckless, the same expression he had when he first came:

"I did it; now you can do whatever you want with me, I don't want to say another word about it."
