Spring and Autumn

Casual Talks of Canglang 175

I recently read an old magazine and saw twelve poems by Li Yinbai of Dantu, inspired by reading Wang Shuiyun's collection. Many of the phrases in the poems describe Shuiyun's life, such as "A qin master grows old in the world, sad when the palace moved north; unable to travel ten thousand rivers and mountains, a heartbroken person sings a heartbroken poem." It is recorded that Wang Shuiyun's name was Yuanliang, a qin artisan at the end of the Song Dynasty. His poems are filled with sorrow and thoughts of the lost nation. After the fall of the Song Dynasty, he went north with the royal family and later returned south as a Daoist priest.

Liu Yiqing, Prince of Linchuan of the Southern and Northern Dynasties' Song Dynasty, wrote the "Shi Shuo Xin Yu," originally in eight volumes. Liu Xiaobiao of the Liang Dynasty annotated and supplemented it, expanding it to ten volumes. The current popular version has only three volumes. It is said that it was reduced to this size by Yan Shu of the Song Dynasty. I rather doubt why Yan Shu would discard such a large portion of it. I suspect that this book might have been mostly lost long before the Song Dynasty.

When I was young, my late father used to show me twenty types of Kangxi coins with different characters on the back, saying to me: "These twenty characters appropriately form a five- or six-character poem, with each character representing a place." The characters are as follows: "Tongfu Lindongjiang, Xuanyuan Sujichang, Ninghenan Guangzhe, Taishan Guiyunzhang." Now, searching through my collection, the collected coins are scattered and incomplete. At this time of fragmented mountains and rivers, when the country cannot be whole, I recall old events, and I feel the same as these coins! (Qin sound)

Recording the Matter of Chen Shaoyang, a Student of the Song Dynasty 176

— Lin Liqin

Liqin, in her youth, read the history of the Song Dynasty and, when she came to the part about Chen Dong, a student from Danyang, who was executed for writing a memorial to the emperor, she would often close the book and sigh, lamenting how, in ancient times, emperors were autocratic, channels of communication were blocked, loyal advice led to death, reaching such extremes! In the early summer of Yihai, I retired from teaching in Loudong and returned home to nurture myself, spending my days with books to pass the long days. When I came across the local chronicles and read Chen Gong's three memorials, I once again closed the book and sighed, greatly surprised that Chen Gong, at a time when treacherous officials were rampant, spoke frankly about current affairs, vehemently denounced powerful and treacherous officials, attacking them with his pen and words, fearlessly criticizing and impeaching them. His behavior inspired both awe and dread. It was fitting that he met his end by axe and execution, ultimately framed by wicked men. However, Chen Gong's loyalty was unwavering, his heart was with the country, and even with the cauldron of boiling water before him, he resolutely chose to speak his mind, encouraging the weak and establishing integrity. He was truly worthy of establishing a model of behavior for the Jin region, so that later generations would admire his integrity and look up to him, worthy to be compared with Jia Yi of Changsha. Since the Republic, foreign powers have invaded and humiliated us, devouring and encroaching upon us like whales and silkworms, growing deeper with each passing day. In past years, the people of the country felt chilled and often lamented the thorny copper camels. The many students, in particular, were deeply concerned about the destruction of the country and the extermination of the people. They have often gathered crowds to shout and petition the government. During the Jingkang period, the Song Dynasty was weak, and the Jurchens invaded, and the empire was as fragile as a thread. Yet the ministers and officials were secretly communicating with the foreign invaders, firmly clinging to the proposal of ceding territory and seeking peace. If the court had one or two people willing to sacrifice themselves for the sake of the country, they would be pushed aside and prevented from holding office, so as not to obstruct their treacherous schemes. Therefore, Chen Gong, as a commoner, led hundreds of fellow students from the Imperial Academy, prostrating themselves before the palace gates and submitting memorials, resolutely pleading for the fate of the nation. At that time, those who heard of it followed suit, reaching a crowd of tens of thousands of people. At that time, those who knocked and kowtowed beneath the palace gates, were spontaneously united, not like the premeditated gatherings of today's people, forming groups to act. However, driven by loyalty and a determination to save the country, both past and present, the motivation is the same. Therefore, I have often thought that Chen Gong's act of prostrating himself before the palace gates during the Jingkang period truly opened the prelude to the petition movement of the Chinese people, advocating for civil rights, unprecedented in history. Was Chen Gong perhaps the initiator of this? According to local chronicles, Chen Gong had a collection of writings in ten volumes, listed in the Siku Quanshu, but it is a pity that I have not seen it. I later heard from a local elder, Mr. Sui Zimeiyuan, that Chen Gong's former residence was in Yuetang in the county, only six or seven li from my home. I assumed that his descendants must have a copy of the collection. I often wanted to visit and borrow it to read, but I have not yet found a way. I happened to discuss this matter with my friend, Mr. Shen Xigong, who readily offered to help and borrowed it from his friend, Mr. Chen Shigang, to return and read it, so that I could enjoy viewing it. I am endlessly grateful to Mr. Shen. I also heard Mr. Shigang say: "Our Chen family, in the past, regarded Shao Yang Gong's third draft memorial from the Jianyan period as a family treasure. After the Taiping Rebellion, we regretfully lost its location. Only the handwriting remains, nothing more." In that case, the circulation of this collection must not be widespread, so I treasure it even more. I quickly asked Mr. Liu Zhizhong to serve as a copyist, and it took a month to complete the task. In addition, those not listed in the collection, as recorded in the local chronicles, were supplemented one by one. In the future, if others are found in other books, they should be further collected, hoping to collect them extensively and compile them anew, and plan to publish them. After the review is complete, I respectfully record a few words to mark it.

The Three Martyrs of Haining 177

— Ru

Haining is a famous place for viewing the tide. Beside the embankment, there are also scenic spots such as the "Zhenhai Pagoda" and the "Zhenhai Iron Ox." People who come to Haining to travel inevitably admire and stroke them. However, the historically significant "Three Martyrs Pagoda" is often overlooked.

The Three Martyrs Pagoda is located beside the sea embankment, built to commemorate the martyr Pang Jingxian, head of the merchant corps during the recovery, and the martyrs Zhu Xizhou and Yu Xilin, members of the corps. At that time, due to the corruption of the Qing court's politics, pirates rose up along the coast of Zhejiang, and merchant ships were often looted by them. The livelihoods of the people were almost interrupted. And the Qing soldiers were lazy by nature and did not want to carry out the conquest, thus arousing the indignation of the head of the Pang corps, leading hundreds of newly trained merchant corps to the front to respond to the enemy. As a result, the pirates were pacified, and the head of the corps and the two members of Zhu and Yu, as well as many ordinary people, also sacrificed their lives for this reason.

This pagoda was built by merchants raising funds in October of the 17th year of the Republic of China. Although it is extraordinarily simple, it is very majestic when viewed from a distance.

Remembering Gu Yewang 178

— Yizhen

During the Chen Dynasty, a great writer, Mr. Gu Xifeng, styled Yewang, stayed in his hometown of Tinglin. Gu was intelligent and studious from an early age, able to write at the age of nine, and once composed a daily rhapsody. At the age of twelve, he followed his father to Jian'an, where he was able to read many classics and historical records, so he was proficient in astronomy, geography, divination, and strange characters. Gu was not only erudite but also skilled in painting, so Gu's talent was very famous in Jian'an.

Later, when Hou Jing rebelled, Yewang observed mourning for his father and returned to Zhao to recruit villagers and follow the righteous army to rescue the capital. Gu was originally very thin and weak, and he also suffered the loss of his father, making him look even more gaunt. However, his heart for defending the country drove him to put on armor, hold a long spear, and perform the heroic act of giving up his pen to join the army. At that time, he explained the righteousness between ruler and subject and the principles of obedience and disobedience to those he led. His righteous indignation was very passionate, and everyone who heard it praised him. Although the result could not be saved, his loyalty and courage are worthy of our admiration.

In his later years, Gu stayed in Tinglin, compiling local chronicles. The "Reading Pile" where he wrote every day still remains in his hometown. Gu died at the age of sixty-two. According to the Huating County Chronicle, his tomb is located southwest of Tinglin, but it is now impossible to find.

Gu's writings are extremely abundant, including the Wang Pian in thirty volumes, the National History Biographies in two hundred volumes, the Biography of Gu, the Jian'an Topography in two volumes, the Outline of General History, the Fushan Picture Preface in one volume, the Catalogue of Auspicious Images in ten volumes, the Sequel to the Dongmingji in one volume, and the Collected Works of Gu Yewang in two volumes.

Little Western Heaven 179

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 23: Eloquently Discussing in the Room, Striving to File a Lawsuit; Pouring Out Old Friendship, Profit Can Make One Forget Grievances

He took them so far back into history before finally taking a seat. When Jia Duocai looked at Mr. Wang, he was wearing a blue cloth lined robe, with a bald head, a long, round, yellow face, and a lot of short, bristly whiskers. Although his clothes were very simple, his eyes were bright and shining, and he was still a worldly-wise man. Jin Ziqiang said that he was a loyal and honest elder, which was a little puzzling. So he nodded to him and said: "Mr. Wang, do you have a lot of land in this city of Xi'an?" Wang Baocheng looked at Jin Ziqiang first before smiling and answering: "What land do I have? It's just common land owned by the clan. The clansmen think that I can talk to the Easterners because I've been to Jiangnan once, so they pushed me to contact Mr. Jin." Jia Duocai said: "But I don't know what place this piece of land is?" Jin Ziqiang said: "It's just outside the North Gate, everyone knows that. That place will soon become a railway station. Our piece of land is very large, and according to insiders, it should be worth twenty thousand yuan there." Jin Ziqiang snatched a laugh and said: "Worth so much money there? Maybe that's ten years from now. Mr. Wang, don't listen to other people's gossip, it's just trying to cheat you. You know I'm a very straightforward person." As he spoke, he passed a cup of tea on the table to him. Then he smiled and said: "Have a cup of tea to moisten your throat first." As he spoke, he went to the bedside, took out a paper box from the net basket, put it on the table, and smiled: "This is chicken cake from Shanghai, although it's a little dry, it's still edible, please try some." As he spoke, he took a piece of chicken cake with two fingers, sent it to Wang Baozheng's hand, and smiled: "We're such good friends, why are you being so polite? We'll have many days of working together in the future." Jia Duocai saw this situation on the side, and his heart was very clear, so he asked Jin Ziqiang in a faint voice: "Brother Jin has already given a fixed price for the land?" Wang Shicheng had just taken a bite of the chicken cake: and immediately replied: "Including that piece of land in Xianyang, Mr. Jin only offered ten thousand yuan." Jin Ziqiang smiled and shook his head and said: "Such a large amount of money, Mr. Wang, do you think it's still very little?" (396)

Doubts from Worthies of Various Provinces 180

— Jiaoxin

This article, published on December 28th of last year, listing the worthies of various provinces throughout history, makes me feel that there are some questionable points, which I would like to discuss with readers.

According to the list, there are three Yan Zhenqing, one from Shaanxi, one from Shandong, and one from Zhejiang. But in history, we only know that there was one Yan Zhenqing in the Tang Dynasty, who was from Zhejiang. Whether his place of origin is mistaken, or whether there are other Yan Zhenqing in Shaanxi and Shandong, is not very clear. However, Piyuanzai states: "Yan Zhenqing of Linyi, Tang Dynasty, styled Qingchen, was the Prince of Pingyuan during the reign of Emperor Xuanzong. When An Lushan rebelled, he alone advocated righteousness to fight against him. After the rebellion was quelled, he was promoted to Minister of Justice and was enfeoffed as Duke of Lu. During the reign of Emperor Dezong, he comforted Li Xilie, held the imperial staff and refused to submit, and was strangled to death, with the posthumous title of Wenzhong. He was good at regular and cursive calligraphy, and his brushstrokes were strong, vigorous, elegant, and outstanding." According to this, Yan Zhenqing was indeed from Linyi County, Zhejiang. Why would there be one each in Shaanxi and Shandong? This is the first point of doubt.

Cao Cao of the Three Kingdoms has been regarded as a treacherous hero for thousands of years; heroes are certainly worthy of worship, but it is not appropriate to choose him as a local worthy when the word "treacherous" is added to the word "hero." Now Anhui has actually listed him, which seems somewhat inappropriate. This is the second point of doubt.

I hope that high-minded people will correct the above two points!

Chronicle of Dragon Sand Mountain 181

— Tianya

A few days ago, I had something to do in Jiangyin. Passing through Huashu Town in the eastern part of the county, I was invited by a friend to stay there for a night and visit several places. During the late Song and early Yuan dynasties, Huashu was a large town along the Yangtze River and a major market for cotton traded from places such as Nantong and Haimen in northern Jiangsu, so it was known as the "Flower Market." Later, sand and soil gradually rose on the south bank of the Yangtze River, and the distance between Huashu and the Yangtze River gradually increased. Now, it is thirty miles away.

Near the north side of the street, there is Dragon Sand Mountain and a Temple of Loyalty. Formally speaking, Dragon Sand Mountain is a small mountain less than ten zhang high, and the Temple of Loyalty is equally desolate and ordinary, not worth visiting, but because these two places are somewhat related to the glorious history of our nation, they should be recorded.

Halfway up Dragon Sand Mountain, there is a patch of grassland about five or six zhang square. This is where our national hero General Yan Yingyuan supported his elderly mother at the end of the Ming Dynasty. Now, the house is naturally gone, but the stone foundation around it is still clearly visible on the ground. General Yan's hometown was originally in Tongxian County, Hebei. He brought his elderly mother to Jiangyin, only to serve as a minor official (similar to the current head of the county public security bureau). He actually took on the heavy responsibility of resisting foreign invasions and saving the country. The result was naturally inevitable death, and all the people of the city, moved by his loyalty and righteousness, also died in defense of it. This is an even more tragic and painful event. Therefore, his heroic spirit and great achievements after his death, like Shi Kefa, who fought to the death in Yangzhou, and Huang Chunyao, who resisted the enemy in Jiading, shine brightly in history and will be remembered forever!

There are many pine trees on the mountain slopes. When the north wind sweeps through, the treetops make a desolate sound. Is that General Yan sighing for our dying nation?

Looking south for hundreds of steps, there is the Temple of Loyalty, where General Yan is enshrined. Because a small school has been established in the temple, the buildings of the entire temple are not very dilapidated. That day was a holiday, and the teachers and students were not in school. The clay statue of the general quietly sat in the alcove in the main hall, wearing a black gauze hat and a red robe, with a solemn face that made people dare not look directly at it. But this temple and statue were built in the Qianlong period of the Qing Dynasty. The clay statue may be somewhat different from his original appearance, but I believe it will not be very different, because the actions and outcomes of all passionate men are mostly the same, just like on the stage, those with green faces and red beards are mostly bandits, and those with white faces are mostly traitors. This symbolic representation may as well exist, giving people a deep impression.

In front of the courtyard there is a guava tree, with lush branches and leaves, and large, fragrant guavas shining with golden light. "The frost-covered skin of the old autumn is covered with honey and wax," which perfectly reflects General Yan's unwavering integrity.

My friend said: "Every year on the general's birthday (February 16th) and death anniversary (August 21st), in the past, all the people in the town would go to the temple to worship. Now, it is desolate. On those days, only some incense and candles are lit, and a few Taoist priests recite scriptures for a day." I think General Yan's greatness does not need incense, candles, and Taoist priests to praise him. It is perfectly appropriate for us to commemorate national heroes, but we must pay attention to the appropriateness of the methods and meanings. For example, if I walked to Dragon Sand Mountain without my friend's guidance, who would recognize that piece of leather was the former residence of a national hero?

When I left Dragon Sand Mountain and the Temple of Loyalty, the setting sun of dusk shone with a wisp of the most bleak light, and the pine wind blew coldly, making my heart feel infinitely desolate and lonely.

East Sea 182

— Shufan

Ten thousand rooms face the eastern sea, Gathering the fierce wind to protect the national gate. Endless are the tears of the Yellow Emperor over ruined tombs, Few are the traces of Kuazhou in the setting sun. The Central Plains yields with ceremony for three homes, Today, survival hangs on two words. Don't look down on Han Bai's armor from that year, He once led expeditions on the river.

Heavy snow flies, the wheels turning for five nights, Spring awakens from a disturbed dream. My chest and lungs, filled with sorrow, will grow horns, Tears flow, the rivers and mountains want to turn to ashes! Family sacrifices must not forget poems to the north, The country is desolate, but the phoenix may not come from the west? The students rush to write memorials, I have no money for a cup of wine.

Peacock Spreading Its Tail Feathers 183

— Qizhong

I have long heard people say that peacocks are competitive, saying that when they see a flower-like girl, they must spread their tail feathers to compete with her in beauty. I have always believed this without a doubt. I have seen many peacocks in the park, but I have never seen a peacock spread its tail feathers. I always thought that the people near me were not beautiful enough in the eyes of the peacocks. Three years ago, in Beiping, I saw the peacocks in Central Park, but they never spread their tail feathers, and I always thought that the people near me were not beautiful enough in the eyes of the peacocks. However, one day, I went to Central Park with several girlfriends, and one of my girlfriends was a "queen" from a certain university, dressed very beautifully, almost everyone had to give her a second look. The queen danced, several girlfriends sang, and the peacocks in the shed only paced back and forth and moved their wings and tail feathers slightly, but they still did not spread their tail feathers. Another time, I walked into Central Park alone, and the peacock happened to be walking outside the shed. I suddenly walked in front of it, spread out my coat, and waved the cane in my hand. The peacock hurriedly walked in, and at that moment it spread its tail feathers. I don't believe that my gray coat was considered beautiful in the eyes of the peacocks. At the same time, I looked at the wings and tail feathers of the peacocks after they spread their tail feathers, and every feather was trembling. I thought that the peacock spreading its tail feathers was not necessarily to compete in beauty, but perhaps it was fear.

In the first half of this year, I had to walk through Dongyang Lane on Dixiwei Road in Hongkou twice a day, either going from home to the company or from the company back home. There are many empty foreign houses in Dongyang Lane. One house is uninhabited, and there is a turkey in the yard, which I think is raised by the owner of the neighboring house. Except for the feathers, I don't see much difference between turkeys and peacocks. I often saw many children throwing stones at this turkey by the iron gate. The turkey spread its tail, spread its wings, and quacked, with every feather trembling. But sometimes when there were no children nearby, it didn't do that. It can be seen that the turkey spreading its tail feathers was entirely due to fear. So, the peacock spreading its tail feathers, not to compete in beauty but to be frightened, seems to have some value in its establishment.

Shi Yousan "Wanted" But Not "Arrested" 184

— Mengruo

Shi Yousan had been wanted by the Central Government, and Yin Rugeng had also been wanted by the Central Government. However, not only are these two men now "wanted" but not "arrested," but they also both have good official positions to assume. One is to be appointed Commander of the Beiping Security Force, and the other is to be appointed Mayor of Tianjin. This is a very comical thing amidst the national chorus of "Down with the traitors!"

Shi is one of China's old warlords. In the past, when he held military power, he was once very prominent. However, he finally failed. But even though he stepped down, he still has considerable latent influence in the north, so he has been quite active recently. Some rumors say that he is organizing some kind of army, or that he is promoting autonomy. However, some people also say that after he relinquished his military power, he has been living in seclusion and does not ask about external affairs. Shi himself has also recently defended himself to others, saying that he has always known only to be content with his lot, but he is often impersonated by others outside, taking illegal actions, causing him to be misunderstood by the people of the country. In fact, Shi's character, his merits and demerits to the country, have their own facts to prove, and enlightened people can see them early on. However, he is now highly valued by Song Zheyuan and will "make a comeback" as Commander of the Beiping Security Force. It is said that Shi once requested to be appointed a member of the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee. The authorities believed that Shi was skilled in "tactics," so they telegraphed the Central Government, requesting that his wanted order be revoked and that he be appointed to the post of Security Commander. I wonder how Shi will use his "tactics" after taking office? We ordinary people may as well monitor him from the sidelines!

What about Yin? He has also been showing off recently because he is said to be a "Japan expert," so the authorities appointed him as the Commissioner of the Ji-Mi District. We don't know much about his talent and knowledge. We only know that since he took office as Commissioner, he has gained the trust of "friendly nations" in diplomatic negotiations. However, this time his ambition is growing. He is not happy with the position of Commissioner, and he boldly raised the banner of rebellion in Tongzhou, relying on his background to seize the 22 counties of the war zone in one fell swoop and become the puppet leader of his pseudo-autonomous government! Unfortunately, the Chinese people today are not very easy to provoke. As soon as Yin's telegram was issued, the cry of "Punish the traitor" resounded throughout the country. Even his brothers were very indignant and advocated that he must be punished. It can be seen that his behavior of "selling out the motherland" is unforgivable. However, he has now become a "number one" important person, interacting very closely with a certain party, and has the potential to "rise rapidly." In the negotiations on the Jidong issue, it is said that the solution is for Yin to abolish the pseudo-organization, and for Song Zheyuan to telegraph the Central Government to request that he be exempted from the wanted order and that he be restored to his former position, or be appointed as Mayor of Tianjin. If this matter can be realized, then although the stock has not been able to get its wish, it is still good to have an official position after the rebellion.

In this day and age, what discipline, what prestige, are not to be taken too seriously. People like Shi Yousan and Yin Rugeng are sinners to the country and despised by the people of the whole country. But they have a great background after all. The authorities can not only do nothing about them, but also have to invite them to take important positions and serve the party and the country. However, once this precedent is set, a group of "active elements" can act recklessly in the future. If they succeed, they will be kings; if they fail, they will still have a place to go. Who would not want to take a risk? No wonder there are so many traitors in our country recently.

Chinese people's actions are always unpredictable!

Old Dream 185

— A Ren

I opened my drowsy eyes, surrounded by pitch black. Shu's hand gently patted my shoulder. In the darkness, I could only see a small thing clinging to my ear like a bug, buzzing and saying to me, "A Ren, wake up! Something's wrong!"

"What?" I yawned, turning over. I could make out Shu's silhouette lying beside me.

Shu was already trembling with fear. Seeing me turn over, she buried her head in my arms without a word.

The situation was indeed strange. Before I closed my eyes and fell asleep, as I couldn't stay awake any longer, the entire cabin was brightly lit by three kerosene lamps. Now, even one lamp was extinguished. I listened carefully. Besides the boatman yelling "Quick, blow out the lights! Quick, blow out the lights!" in another cabin, Shu's mother and several old women were huddled in a corner of the cabin, chanting anxiously in low voices, "Amitabha, Amitabha."

Shu raised her wide eyes, shining in the darkness, and said to me, "Just as I closed my eyes to sleep, the boat suddenly shook, swaying back and forth a few times, and then stopped. We were just wondering what was happening when the boatman ran over from the stern, telling us to quickly blow out the lights and ordering us not to make any noise. He gave the same orders in the other cabins. See, everyone is shrinking back, waiting for an unforeseen disaster to befall us." After Shu finished speaking, she tightly gripped my hands and buried her head in my arms again.

Indeed, the sound of the engine was gone. The boat seemed to be asleep, lazily lying there. The rushing of the river water against the sides was like its heavy snoring, echoing in the terrifying darkness, pressing down on everyone's breath.

I was now fully awake. The old women's hurried, panting "Amitabha"s were truly laughable, but a sudden, unexpected terror, in the pitch-black, silent night, was strangely stabbing at my nerves.

Suddenly, one or two cannon shots rang out in the distance, shaking clearly in the deathly silent sky. I couldn't tell if they were from our country or the enemy, but I knew that we were already stopped in the war zone.

Shu and I sat up and pulled back the curtain on the small round window. Looking out over the vast, silver-scaled river surface, in that dark gray corner to the east, a storm of epochal significance was descending. That thunder, that lightning, that red fire, the generosity and anger vaguely visible in the fire, the broken limbs sacrificed for us, and the red blood rising with heat... the terror that had just assailed my nerves slowly disappeared at this moment.

The hurried panting of "Amitabha, Amitabha" gradually moved closer to me. Turning around, in the moonlight, I saw Shu's mother's anxious expression, her dry hands trembling as they held out a long robe.

"Mr. Xu, quickly take off your Western clothes and put on this robe. When the soldiers come later, they won't suspect you're a student and take you away."

I took the robe from her hand and looked at Shu's face. Shu's trembling mouth and eyes also pleaded for me to quickly change my clothes. Seeing that pitiful and shameful cowardly appearance, I couldn't help but laugh.

"If I really am captured and killed by the soldiers, Shu, what are you going to do?" I asked Shu with a smile.

"I will never marry for the rest of my life!" Her voice carried a touch of solemnity.

"Never marry for the rest of your life?" Such an outdated, feudal idea was so deeply entwined in Shu. Why not immediately think of uniting the masses to avenge me? I began to feel melancholic.

For four years, this melancholy, like light smoke, has always, always lingered in my heart.

Night at Guanyin Bridge 186

— Yun Qi

——Be careful at night; don't fall into a dead sleep, eh!

When it was time to sleep, Zhang, the head porter, came back to give this instruction again, his purplish-brown face covered with a layer of sternness.

The oil lamp dimly illuminated the contours of everyone's faces. Outside the window, the mountain stream sounded like an army of thousands hidden away. In the distance, an occasional echo, like the howl of a wild ghost, made everyone's hair stand on end. Everyone shared a common thought: "This terrifying night at Guanyin Bridge!"

The people traveling together gathered to hold a meeting. The air was filled with intense hope contained within the tension!

——We must divide into shifts to sleep and watch over the entire night! This is the final decision.

Page 20

The first shift was assigned to A Huang, Xiao Liu, and Xiang Sen—three hours per shift.

Given the circumstances, we should naturally be able to sleep soundly, but the air of terror stimulated our heartstrings. Who could possibly fall asleep? Listening, listening, we heard the three men's disordered footsteps in the courtyard, pacing back and forth. No one said anything. The night was as silent as the dead primordial era.

It was the time of the waning moon; the moon was invisible. The courtyard was as black as pitch. Sometimes, when the three of them stumbled on an unfamiliar path or bumped into the carrying pole or some other miscellaneous object, the sound would startle those lying in bed, subconsciously making them think of the arrival of bandits, or perhaps it would really be that way.

From under the eaves came a burst of snoring. The porters' expressions of "nothing else matters except myself" were actually quite endearing. They didn't think about anything beyond themselves. What filled their hearts was the resolution to find a way to live tomorrow.

The little desk clock clearly struck twelve. A Huang and the others handed over the shift. The second shift was supposed to be Chong, Lao Tie, and me, along with Broad-Mouthed Yang.

——How was it? No trouble, right?

——If there was trouble, that would be terrible. Just listening to any small sound would shatter our courage!

Without allowing any excuses, I shouldered the task. I thought to myself that the first half of the night would be easier to get through; the second half, though? That was hard to say. Bandits would mostly appear after midnight, wouldn't they? They would all have murderous faces. If they really appeared, then... I shouldn't think about that terrible scene!

——After our shift is over, it will be almost dawn. How will we be able to climb the mountain then?

This was indeed a question worth raising. The mountain road was so rugged and uneven, and it was the hot season. The weight on the porters' shoulders would often cause the purple-red blood streaks to stick to both ends of the bamboo pole. In this desolate, exiled region, they earnestly hoped that the travelers could show them some sympathy and climb some of the steep mountain roads themselves.

——Those on duty can sleep while walking on the road, A Huang said, suggesting that the original weight be reduced and distributed among the other burdens.

In the back courtyard, Lao Tie and I were bored, each occupying a corner and pacing around. The mosquitoes here were truly fierce. A swarm would fly over, humming a pleasant little tune in their mouths. Soon, our skin would be unbearably itchy. After rubbing it with a towel, we would feel as if we were burning up with heat.

Suddenly, there were footsteps on the street, mixed with some indistinguishable voices. Immediately, the three of us gathered together and hid beside the front counter. Slowly, they got closer and closer. Judging from the sound, there were more than five people.

——It's here, it's here. We haven't been here before! said someone with a strangely rough accent to the others.

The three of us started to tremble. How should we deal with them? Being soft wouldn't work; being hard—they had more people, and we had so few weapons. How could we resist them? Fear? Retreat? We were completely trapped in a circle of bewilderment.

In the blink of an eye, several people had already entered the shop, shining flashlights all around. The things hanging down from their waists—weren't those Mauser pistols for showing off? In the mutual illumination of the flashlights, I noticed that the people were not wearing headscarves or any tight-fitting jackets. From the symbols on their collars, I realized that they were local militiamen, charged with maintaining security.

——Whose sedan chairs and belongings are these? someone asked.

——Ours, Lao Tie jumped out to tell him, also saying some of the usual things about where we came from and where we were going.

He didn't seem to believe Lao Tie's words very much. In his mind, he probably thought that the sudden appearance was impossible. Afterward, he looked at the flag stuck on the carrying basket, nodded, said some polite words, and left.

The sound of footsteps disappeared in the distance. The long street was still as silent as before.

We quietly stepped back into the backyard. The mosquitoes were still playing their little tunes, the grasshoppers were singing loudly, and a few drifting clouds floated westward. The sky was entering the stage of dawn.

Rushing the Journey 187

— Ye Lai

In the evening, the villages and towns of the South lightly wear the weary sunlight, which contains boundless coolness. The villagers, in pairs and in groups, who had entered the market have already taken their goods home sparsely. The markets and narrow streets have become quiet. We, a group of young people, could no longer linger in this small town, and were preparing to go to the area of Kaiping.

Stepping out of the Baisha market is a long path through fields and caves. The golden plains and bamboo forests gradually became dark. Gusts of cold wind swept across our hearts. In this countryside, which was quickly rolling into darkness, our group of strangers couldn't help but feel anxious:

"It's still a three-hour bus ride to Xiangang! It's getting dark!" the leader said.

When we ran to the bus station, there was still a bus parked there. The driver and the people in the factory seemed to dislike us, frowning and muttering at us:

"The bus isn't running. You didn't come earlier. It's getting dark."

"Why isn't it running? Aren't you helping the National Salvation Propaganda Team? We must get to Xiangang!" Guan Jun said in their local dialect, and then comforted us, "Don't worry about these profiteers! We'll sit in the carriage and won't leave until the bus leaves. Victory is ours."

Amidst the muttering, three passengers boarded the bus. We breathed a sigh of relief and squeezed into the carriage. The driver reluctantly started the bus, but it drove very slowly. The uneven road threw the bus, along with us, up and down. Our hungry stomachs were also turning somersaults. At that time, looking out of the carriage window, all we saw was a hazy night that had tightly enveloped the mountains and fields. The sky became darker and darker, and our spirits became more and more tense.

At a fork in the road, the bus suddenly stopped, which startled us a lot. Then, the three passengers got off because they had reached their destination and left triumphantly. The skinny driver also breathed a sigh of relief cunningly:

"The bus can't go any further. Our bus only goes this far. The next section of the road belongs to another company. Our company has no right to drive on it. There will be a bus coming in a while."

When we saw this situation, we couldn't help but feel angry. Guan Jun shouted:

"What are you talking about? Are you trying to deceive us? Let's drive the bus ourselves!"

However, no one knew how to drive a bus, and in this dark night, in the wilderness where we couldn't see anything at all, how could we rush the journey? So, we roared with anger:

"Let's smash this bus! We can run there. It's only twenty li from here to Xiangang." Then, we were about to take action and pressure the driver: "Do you want to be a slave of a fallen country? Don't you know about the loss of the Northeast and the fighting in Shanghai? You're ashamed to be a Guangdong person!"

Shouting; the fire of us young people started to burn.

At this time, we looked . . . what did we see? The black masses of the distant mountains and fields . . . unfolded in darkness. The whistling wind . . . The weeds on both sides were just shrinking back . . . There were also a few light barks of dogs coming from the distant mountain villages. A wave of terror rose in our hearts, as if we were worrying about having stepped into a den of robbers. Looking at everyone's tense faces, full of anger and terror, in the darkness, some were still trembling.

The bus still sped towards the black, paint-like mountains and fields, jumping up and down, tossing our hearts. We were still shrinking back in the carriage, looking at each other, not having felt any relief from the terror.

As if we had found light, when we arrived at Xiangang, in the quiet station, under the dim yellow light, we saw a group of children and two teachers waiting for us. Moreover, they were shouting:

"Welcome the National Salvation Propaganda Team!"

The pleasant enthusiasm in our hearts started to burn again.

Ballad Singing 190

Xu Wenbi's Opening Piece

City Sound (1340) 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM Opening Piece "New Year Song"

Light soup and spring breeze harmonize, ten thousand families set off firecrackers and ten thousand families beat gongs. The New Year's fourth day follows the fifth day. The Five Roads Wealth Gods are greeted aplenty. Fortune, prosperity, and longevity are all there. Chicken, fish, and pork fill the plates. Pine needles, cypress branches, and evergreen leaves—it is essential to bid farewell to the old year and welcome the gods. Ten thousand households and thousands of doors all respect and value them. The Roadhead Bodhisattva has no skill. Poor families may not personally arrive, but Lucky Profit and Wealth Summoning substitute them. With candles and incense, they often arrive. Without tea or wine, they are cold and aloof. The True Yi Xuan Tan is ultimately afraid to come. Gold, comfort, and satisfaction do not covet the picture. My family is receiving the Wealth Gods today. I do not care about the Dragon Boat Festival on the fifth day. I heard that Zhong Kui is marrying off his younger sister. The Roadhead Bodhisattva asks for a wife in verse. From this, it is known that Doctor Zhong's closest kin are brother-in-law and brother-in-law both call each other. Wife's brother, younger sister's husband, naturally there are matters to discuss and help with. Surely they will call their brother-in-law on their birthday, arranging a public share to play songs and music. The Ministry of Wealth and Silver also has a share. Everyone definitely does not look down on me. A great source of wealth comes quickly like a shuttle.

Cheng Fangzhou, Li Liansun, Mao Jiashu

Hua Mei (1060) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM Opening Piece "New Year"

Yesterday the Roadhead was received a lot, and today everyone is drinking Tusu wine. Fathers are kind, sons are filial, families are blessed. People are safe, things are rich, and interest is abundant. Young masters and grandsons ride dappled horses. Fair ladies and women worship Amitabha. Zhuangyuan picture, promotion picture, Lantern Festival running horse show, ten-course gongs. Congratulations are sent with name cards. Etiquette is diligent, how dare one be negligent. Everyone says that the Jiangzhe province is the norm, and the reputation of literature and relics allows the three Wu. Wealth and poverty are determined by heaven, what does it matter. Countless illuminated boats pass through Shantang. There is singing and music everywhere in the streets. The sound of the song slowly floats and sings in the wind, singing out the most wonderful feelings of longing. Sixteen thousand is easy to pass. Life is only suitable for living in Suzhou. Until now, beautiful sentences praise Dongpo.

Du Wenkui, Zhou Jianhong, Big Red Robe

Sino-Western (1040) Midnight 12:15 AM to 1:00 AM Opening Piece "Playful Spring Words"

All day long, I search for spring but cannot find it. It turns out it is illusory and shapeless. Cold plums happily announce the arrival of spring first. Spring arrives, and the scenery of Jiangnan is new. I say, the great earth's spring truly has feet. It leaves the spring emperor to live in the spring city alone. But that, the spring breeze in the village is chilly, and the spring cold is heavy. Spring rain is continuous, and spring hatred is deep. I am exactly, the spring painting is sleepy, and the spring mood is lazy. It is good to let that, the spring shade secretly protect the crabapple heart. I am only afraid that, the wind and rain will come at night, and the spring flowers will weep. Spring is on the branches, afraid to hear the crossbow. Until this morning, the spring sun brings warmth, and the spring atmosphere moves. Boundless spring fills the garden. Cut vegetables after the rain add spring bamboo shoots. Link the spring plate with non-pungent spices. It is just right, the newly split Xiangtou spring brew is ripe. The spring officials' peach and plum feast is at the door. At times, go out to seek traveling spring companions. Rain washes the spring suburbs, and green grass grows. I only fear the muddy spring will prevent us from slipping. I see, the green spring clogs imprint fragrant moss. Gazing far, the spring water of the green waves rises with the help of poles. The light black spring mountains fill the city. I also see, at the corner of the spring flag where wine is sold. Investigate flowers, spring is warm, sell tin sounds. Only because, the spring is late in March, the oriole dreams. Spring news is frequently transmitted by island warbling sounds. Spring clouds are empty and sad. The willows rely on each other, short and long pavilions. What can be done, the mad bees and butterflies are spring and mischievous. Flowers fall in the late spring, unattached feelings. I only blame that, until death, spring silkworms are bound by silk. Spring clothes want to be wet and touched by dust. I worry that, spring returns, spring easily urges people to age. I fail to live up to the spring light, and I feel sad. After the fallen flowers cover the ground, spring is gone. Spring sunshine is happily staying, and the years are startling. At that time, flowers bloom and fade, spring is masterless. I only feel, when spring swallows return, where to seek. Since ancient times, grieving over spring, Du Mu. Spring sorrows are obscure and most soul-destroying. Try to ask him, whose dream of spring belongs to.

Remainder Sound

Yao Fengjun's great work said, "One Light's public performance is related to the effect of air." But I do not know what Yao Fengjun based it on. Please Yao Mr. give a detailed reply. (Wang Qianying)

The Fei Hong Bimonthly published by the Fei Hong Music Research Society, Volume 2, Issue 1 is the Innovation Issue. The main contents include Dong Jia's "Society Words" discussing togetherness and self-reliance, and Wang Ju's "Confidant Collection," etc., which are all carefully crafted works. The supplement "Freedom" is edited by Mr. Wang Shiying, and the content includes the trends of the literary and art circles, Wang Zhengyu's creative novel "Her Destiny," You Ren's "Husband and Wife," and Zheren's "Little Zhang," etc. The publication sells for foreign cents per issue, and the annual subscription including postage is three foreign dollars. The address is No. 2, Wen'anfang, Panjia Street, Old North Gate. Chen Mo has not joined the Luye Society.

The Fei Hong Bimonthly, Volume 2, Issue 1 Innovation Issue is about to be published.

The Era Opera Society is about to be established. The hosts are Zheren and Manqing.

It is said that the Great Daily News will stop publishing "Silver Song."

Junping's recent work "The Secret History of Singing Stars" will be published in "Silver Song." (Above by Shiying)

Movie News

Anecdotes of "Wedding Night" 191

"Wedding Night" is the most valuable production of Yihua Company in 1936. It is Yue Feng's most elaborate and greatest masterpiece after "Escape."

"Wedding Night" suggests the most personal problems of two young men and women, but one is a forced marriage oppressed by autocratic forces, and the other is a free love built on materialism.

"Which young girl does not cherish spring?" "Wedding Night" grasps this point, dissects the psychological state of a young girl in puberty, and the actions of love and desire induced by it, so "Wedding Night" is equal to a youth reader, and also equal to a love scripture.

"Wedding Night" is also like a pot of candied fruit, a bottle of aged vinegar, a plate of pepper, and a dish of mustard sauce, both sweet and sour, both bitter and spicy.

"I'd rather die than be unfree!" Yuan Meiyun struggles in "Wedding Night" for the sake of love and the evil environment, but in the end, she is still a lamb unable to resist!

"Wedding Night" has extremely complicated love tangles, such as Yuan Meiyun and Wang Yin, Wang Yin and Lin Ling, Lin Ling and Zhang Boli, then Yuan Meiyun and Guan Hongda, Guan Hongda and Zhou Xuan, Zhou Xuan and Liu Li, etc. As the plot unfolds, these vortexes of love are like wind and waves, with layers of waves and infinite changes.

"Wedding Night" is a film that everyone should watch, with extremely good intentions. Young ladies and loving couples will feel as comfortable as eating a cup of ice cream after watching it, and their hearts will bloom. As for older ladies, after watching it, it is like eating a piece of sandalwood olive, the more you chew, the more flavorful it is, and the more you chew, the sweeter it is.

Qingdao Scenery 192

The story of "Peach Blossoms After the Calamity" takes place in Qingdao. It writes about the vicissitudes of this fairyland-like idyllic resort, from Qingdao's German lease period, through Japanese jurisdiction, to China's reception and reunification. The film has changed three different national emblems. --Here, we see the joys and sorrows of people, and we also see the cicadas' cicadas' state affairs, and we see the old dreams of the rise and fall of this embroidered country.

A Tomboyish Girl 193

Xu Jian—a tomboyish girl. In today's world of song and dance, she can be considered one of the most eye-catching figures. She not only possesses a talent for singing and dancing but also has all the necessary qualities of a film actor. In the past, she has appeared on the silver screen, although she was not able to fully showcase her talents. However, people generally hold a kind of hope for her. She has been chosen for an important role in Sun Yu's "Back to Nature." We believe: past events have proven that under the direction of Sun Yu, a new actor often achieves great success.

"A Comprehensive View of the Rift Between Li Jinhui and Xu Lai" Published 194

A collection of discussions on life issues by writer Xu Wancheng. "Recently Published: A Comprehensive View of the Rift Between Li Jinhui and Xu Lai." Details are given regarding the backgrounds and character of Li and Xu, and the process of their relationship, marriage, and breakup. Price: one dime per copy. Published by Longwen Bookstore, Da Nan Men, Shanghai. Mail orders will be sent with postage included.
